Opening of the National Training Conference 53

The National Training Conference held its opening ceremony at 9:00 AM on the 15th in the auditorium of the Central Party Headquarters. Present were Central Committee members, representatives from party headquarters in various provinces and special municipalities, general branches overseas, special party headquarters of various armies and railway bureaus, officials from various central departments and councils, and representatives from various courts and ministries, totaling approximately six to seven hundred people. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek presided. After the ceremony, Vice Minister of Training He Yingqin reported (Minister Dai Chuanxian was receiving medical treatment in Shanghai due to illness), stating that the Party bears the mission of leading the masses in various tasks, and training is particularly important. In the past, there were inevitable errors in the training of the masses, which caused mass organizations to deviate from the right track. Therefore, based on the plan decided by the Third National Congress, this conference was convened to study good guidelines and seek to improve facilities during this period of political tutelage, to improve the livelihood and education of the masses, to strengthen the belief in the Three Principles of the People, and all factual needs, to plan in detail and serve as a guide. Therefore, the conference has great significance: (1) to understand the work status of party headquarters at all levels; (2) to remedy the shortcomings of past work and seek comprehensive and sound training, so that the Party and the masses have a spirit of unity, and are not scattered. For example, spiritual education should enable young men and women to have correct beliefs, so as to cultivate the moral abilities necessary for the people during the period of political tutelage, or vigorously carry out cooperation and thrift movements to improve the social economy, so as to consolidate the foundation of the Three Principles of the People. These are all the most important plans at present. It is hoped that based on the plan of the Third Plenary Session and referring to the experience of more than a year, the conference will gather together and achieve good results, so that all levels of party headquarters and the masses can communicate and unite, respond in a chain, and all soldiers in the armies can understand the spirit of the Party, promote hard work, and focus on their work. I am deeply honored. Then, Chiang Kai-shek, representing the Central Committee, gave an instruction, stating that the Party's strength has already spread throughout the country, but reactionary forces still continue to arise. Party members in various places cannot use their work efficiency to promote the elimination of the reactionaries. This must be attributed to the shortcomings in training, which must be examined and remedied. Before the Qing Dynasty, when the Party could not be public, there was not much training, but the party members received a few instructions from the Premier, or a few articles, and they were able to imprint them in their minds and fight to the death. Later, the party affairs were made public, the scope became larger, and there were more party members, and training became more difficult. Generally, young people have many misunderstandings about revolutionary theory, and the Communist Party and all the reactionaries are also mixed in, confusing the public, causing the people to not know what to do. Now, it is urgent to concentrate talents and carefully study how to make the people's faith firm and not be incited by the reactionaries, so that the foundation of the Party will not be shaken. The most important points in training work: (1) It is necessary to follow a certain step, starting on a small scale and gradually seeking to expand it. If the party headquarters in each province train 200 cadre party members each year for each county and district party headquarters to be responsible for training the masses in each county, the effect will definitely be great. (2) The orders and slogans of the Central Party Headquarters must be implemented in the coal departments at all levels and the general public, so that they can be jointly observed. If the party headquarters is equal to the yamen, the committee member is equal to the official, and the party member is equal to the gentry, it will flow into corruption, and the future of the Party will be unimaginable. (3) Training should be based on party education as a principle, so that the military and civilians are all affected. Therefore, training in schools and troops should be more emphasized than ordinary training. If the party and the military and the people can be consistent in spirit, then even if there are a small number of reactionaries who are making trouble, it will not be difficult to make them eliminate themselves, etc. Then, Education Minister Chiang Meng-lin finished his speech, the ceremony was completed, a group photo was taken, and the meeting adjourned.

Ministry of Foreign Affairs Reports Recent Diplomacy 54

Yesterday afternoon (the 14th), the Ministry of Foreign Affairs sent Bao Jing'an to the Central Broadcasting Radio Station to report on recent diplomacy. The report is recorded as follows:

"There are several diplomatic matters this week that are worth reporting. First, let's talk about the Sino-Russian issue. Since the Boli Preliminary Conference decided to mutually release prisoners of war and overseas Chinese, China released all the Russian overseas Chinese who were previously detained in the Songbei Detention Center in Harbin. However, the Soviet Union has not yet fully fulfilled its obligations. According to a recent report from the German Embassy, there are still 45 overseas Chinese detained in Vladivostok who refuse to be released. At the same time, the German Foreign Ministry also received the same report, and stated that the overseas Chinese who have been released have also been subjected to abuse, their assets have not been returned, and they have been subjected to various difficulties in issuing exit passports, causing our overseas Chinese to suffer all kinds of hardships. The German Foreign Ministry has telegraphed the German Ambassador to Russia to actively negotiate, etc. It is most regrettable that Russia disregards international credibility. The German Embassy now believes that the German consul in Vladivostok is too busy to represent China's interests for a long time, and hopes that we will send personnel to Vladivostok as soon as possible to handle matters. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has ordered Xu Xiong, the Consul General stationed in Vladivostok, to return to his post immediately. As for the date of the formal Sino-Russian conference, it will have to wait until our plenipotentiary representative, Mo Dehui, arrives in Harbin and contacts the Russian side before it can be decided.

The second matter is the dissolution of the Kuomintang branch in Singapore by the new Governor-General of Singapore, Clementi. This matter has already aroused the attention of the national people, and questions have also been raised in the British Parliament about this matter, which shows the seriousness of the matter. On February 20, the Governor of Singapore, Clementi, invited the second executive and supervisory committee members of the Singapore General Branch to the Governor's Office for a discussion. He believed that the existence of the Kuomintang branch hindered British sovereignty and gave a deadline of one month to abolish all party branches in Singapore. After receiving the report, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs immediately telegraphed the Minister to the United Kingdom, Shi Zhaoji, and the Consul General to Singapore, Tang Liu, to file a serious protest separately. The British Foreign Ministry has now telegraphed Clementi for inquiries, and believes that it is inappropriate for the Governor to handle this matter without first reporting it. This matter can be expected to be resolved soon. Regarding the suppression of party members in the Dutch East Indies, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has telegraphed the Consul General in Java to actively negotiate.

The third is the negotiation to abolish the forced labor of Chinese laborers in Dutch Sumatra. According to the laws of the Dutch East Indies, there are regulations on compulsory labor for Easterners. There were such regulations in various places in the past. Recently, the islands of Java have been cancelled, but the various places in Sumatra have not yet been cancelled. In the Eastern region, there is a so-called compulsory fire fighting system. All overseas Chinese are designated by the local authorities to go to the scene to fight the fire if there is a fire in the area. If they do not go, they will be fined no more than 25 guilders, or detained for no more than 25 days. In the Raha area, overseas Chinese should pay 15 guilders per year for road repair tax and night watch tax, otherwise they will be subjected to forced labor. Now the road repair tax, etc., has been cancelled through the active negotiations of our country's consuls. As for the compulsory fire fighting system in the east, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has ordered Consul Tang of Jukang to actively negotiate, and it can be hoped that it will be cancelled soon.

The fourth is the issue of treaty revision. The Treaty of Friendship between China and Cuba is now being actively negotiated by Ling Bing, the Minister to Cuba, with the Cuban government. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has presented a request to the National Government to appoint Minister Ling as the plenipotentiary representative for signing the Treaty of Friendship and Commerce. The Greek government has already ratified the Sino-Greek Treaty. Wang Zhengting, the Foreign Minister, and Song Ziwen, the Finance Minister, and Shigemi Mitsuru, the Japanese Chargé d'Affaires, have agreed on a draft of the Sino-Japanese Customs Agreement at the diplomatic residence in Sakae-Wan. After consulting the governments of the two countries, it can be formally signed. The content of the agreement reported in the newspapers is not accurate. Regarding the issue of recovering the leased territory of Weihaiwei, the British Minister Lampson has sent the draft agreement to London for instructions. The instructions from the British government have not yet been received. After the instructions arrive, the agreement can be formally signed. Regarding the Sino-US Arbitration Treaty, the term has now expired. The Minister to the United States, Wu Chaoshu, is negotiating with the United States to renew it. A few days ago, Minister Wu sent the draft renewal treaty to the Ministry for review. The Ministry believed that there were still inappropriate places in the articles, and telegraphed the Minister to negotiate amendments with the US government. Now, Minister Wu has telegraphed that the US government has agreed to amend the points. After receiving the report, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs telegraphed Minister Wu, ordering him to proceed with the signing procedures. Fifth, two Sino-US pending cases have been resolved. These two cases occurred entirely in 1923. One was that in May 1923, American soldiers shot and killed a coolie, Zhang Lin, in Ji County, Hebei Province. After repeated negotiations by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the offending soldiers were sentenced to life imprisonment by the American military court, and the victim's family was compensated with US$1,000. The other case was that in February 1923, American soldiers were target shooting in Hankou, and a stray bullet accidentally killed a child, Tang Huan. The victim's family has now been compensated with US$100. These two sums have been handed over to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs by the American Minister Johnson for forwarding to the victim's family. These two cases seem to have been delayed for too long on the surface. In fact, the American government pays great attention to the budget. No matter how much extra expenditure, it must be approved by Congress before it can be allocated. Because there are too many procedures for turnover, it has been delayed until recently before it was concluded.

Sixth, regarding the issue of protecting foreign nationals in China, several very unfortunate things have happened recently. One is that three Finnish missionaries were kidnapped by bandits in Guangdong. One is that Dutch missionaries were robbed in Anhui. One is that the French consul in Longzhou, Guangxi, was taken away by the Communist bandits. In addition to telegraphing the responsible authorities in each province to do their best to rescue them, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has also transferred the matter to the Ministry of Military Affairs, requesting that all armies and divisions in the country must pay attention to the safety of the lives and property of foreigners in the future and provide extra protection. The Ministry of Military Affairs has now transferred the matter to the garrisons in each province to comply with the instructions.

Seventh, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Judicial Administration are now negotiating the recovery of the Shanghai French Concession Mixed Court. Regarding this issue, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has already notified the French Minister, and the method of recovery can be formally discussed soon. In addition, China's activities in the international arena are also worth reporting. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs received a notification from the Secretariat of the League of Nations, stating that the International Arbitration Security Committee has scheduled a meeting in Geneva on the 24th of this month, and has invited China to send a representative to attend. Our country's representative has not yet been appointed. The 14th International Labor Conference is scheduled to be held in Geneva on June 10th, and China will also send a representative to participate. The French Embassy reported that the First International Microbiology Congress is scheduled to be held in Paris on July 20th this year. The Secretary-General of the Congress has formally sent a letter to our country, inviting us to send an official representative to attend at that time. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has sent a letter to the Ministry of Health for review. Livide, the head of the French Aviation Propaganda Committee, formally notified Gao Lu, our Minister to France, that the Committee has scheduled to convene the First International Aviation Safety Congress in Paris on December 12th this year to discuss the scientific and practical safety of aviation. All countries in the world will be invited to attend, and our country is invited to sponsor it. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs is now reviewing the plan with the Ministry of Military Affairs and Communications. The International Statistical Conference is scheduled to be held in Japan in September this year, and we have formally sent a letter inviting our country to send a representative to attend. At that time, our country will send personnel from the competent statistical authority to participate. The Czechoslovak representative notified our country, inviting us to send a representative to attend the First International Criminal Punishment Conference. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has now asked the Judicial Yuan to review it."

Gu Zhutong Leads Troops to Arrive in Ji'nan 55

Jinan, 12th: According to reports from Jinan, the Central Army's Second Division has now deployed six regiments to Jinan, with the remainder still en route. The division's supply stations and rear hospitals have also arrived. Gu Zhutong, the Sixteenth Route Army Commander-in-Chief, arrived in Jinan by special train from Xuzhou at 12:05 PM today (the 12th), along with the heads of the eight departments of the General Headquarters. When the special train entered the station, military police were on high alert in the vicinity. Chen Tiaoyuan dispatched Ruan Zhaochang, commander of the Fifty-fifth Division, and Zhao Jingshi, the mayor of Jinan, to welcome him at the station. Before Gu's arrival, the Sixteenth Route Army General Headquarters had already been set up in the Jinan commercial district's Chamber of Commerce. After disembarking, Gu went directly to his headquarters to rest, and then to the General Headquarters of the Punitive Expeditionary Army's General Reserve Force to meet with Chen Tiaoyuan for a long discussion. It is said that after Gu's troops arrive in Shandong, they will be stationed between Jinan and Tai'an. Currently, the Fourth Brigade and Sixth Brigade have arrived in Jinan. The headquarters of the Fourth Brigade is located at the Gongshun Inn on Dama Road, and the headquarters of the Sixth Brigade is located in Xinzhuang. The Seventh Regiment of the Fourth Brigade is stationed in Duandian, the Eighth Regiment in Zhangzhuang, and the Ninth Regiment in Shierliqiao. The Tenth and Twelfth Regiments of the Sixth Brigade are both stationed in Xinzhuang, while the Eleventh Regiment is stationed in Wangguanzhuang, west of the city. The Fourth Brigade's medical team is stationed at the western end of Duandian, and the Sixth Brigade's field hospital is located at the Dechang Factory on Weiliu Road in the commercial district. It is reported that the headquarters of the Fourth Branch of the General Supply Station is located at Tianqiao. It is said that a comprehensive deployment will be made after all of Gu's troops arrive.

Another report from the Central News Agency, Jinan, 10th: Although Yan Xishan has announced his resignation, Fu Zuoyi's troops in the Cangzhou and Lianzhen areas have not yet withdrawn. To strengthen the defense of Shandong, the Central Government has specially dispatched Gu Zhutong's Second Division to assist the Shandong Army. As of today (the 10th), five trains of Gu's troops have arrived. The first train carried Wang Jingjiu, commander of the Ninth Regiment of the Fourth Brigade of the Second Division. The entire regiment arrived in Jinan at 6:45 AM on the 9th, disembarked immediately, and marched to Luokou, then to Shierliqiao on the south bank of the Yellow River. The second train arrived in Jinan at 7:30 AM, carrying the entire Seventh Regiment of the Fourth Brigade of the Second Division, led by Commander Hou Kesheng. After disembarking, they marched to Duandian near Luokou to garrison. The third train, carrying Lou Jingyue, the commander of the Fourth Brigade, along with a battalion of special forces and the brigade headquarters, arrived in Jinan at 9:20 AM. The fourth train arrived in Jinan at 3:15 PM, carrying the entire regiment of Mei E, the deputy commander of the Eighth Regiment of the Fourth Brigade. Both of these trains went to Zhangzhuang, and the brigade headquarters was set up in Zhangzhuang. After disembarking, Lou Jingyue, the commander of the Fourth Brigade, went to the General Headquarters to meet with Chen Tiaoyuan to discuss everything. The fifth train arrived in Jinan this morning, carrying the first and second battalions of Wang Zhonglian, the commander of the Eleventh Regiment of the Fourth Brigade. After disembarking, they marched to Wangguanzhuang on the south bank of the Yellow River in Luokou to garrison. The remaining units of Gu's division are continuously departing. Gu Zhutong himself will also arrive in Jinan soon. It is said that after Gu was appointed by the Central Government as the Commander-in-Chief of the Sixteenth Route Army, the Second Division of Gu, the Fifty-second Division of Ye Kaixin, and the Provisional Third Division of Liu Zhendian were placed under the command of the Sixteenth Route Army. Currently, more than three regiments of Gu's troops have arrived in Jinan, and the remaining troops and Ye Kaixin's division are in Xuzhou, preparing to depart. After receiving orders, Liu Zhendian, in addition to leaving a portion to defend Yantai, will concentrate the remaining troops in Huimin and Putai to await further instructions. The Sixteenth Route Army General Headquarters will be located in the former Foreign Affairs Office on Xiaowei Erlu in Jinan. The army will be responsible for the defense between Jinan and Tai'an. Ruan Zhaochang, the commander of the Fifty-fifth Division, recently returned to Jinan to consult with Chen Tiaoyuan, the chairman of the provincial government. He stated that the division currently has only Yue Shengxuan's 163rd Brigade stationed in Yanzhou and Wenshang, while the remaining brigades, such as Li Songshan's 164th Brigade, are stationed in Pingyuan and Yucheng, and Zhang Bin's 165th Brigade is stationed in Jinan. Therefore, the division headquarters must be moved to Jinan for convenient command. This was submitted to the Central Government for approval. Today, Xu Weimin, the chief of staff of the division, has returned to Jinan from Yanzhou with all the staff of the division headquarters. The division headquarters will be temporarily located in Jinan, and its future destination has not yet been determined. The defense of the Yanzhou and Lincheng areas has been filled by Chen Xiaosi's Second Security Brigade.

Important News II

Ge Jing'en Hosts the Press 56

Announces the Qingdao Municipal Plan

Ge Jing'en, the mayor of Qingdao, hosted Chinese and foreign journalists at the Municipal Government Auditorium at 4:30 PM on the 11th, with over forty people in attendance. Ge announced the Qingdao municipal operation plan, saying, "I should have visited everyone upon my arrival in Qingdao, but due to the busy schedule, I have invited you all here for a talk. Please forgive any shortcomings. Since I arrived in Qingdao, several reporters have asked about the Qingdao governance policy. I was unable to respond at the time, and I have no personal policy. All municipal facilities will be handled in accordance with the municipal policy set by the Central Government. However, there are several aspects of the current municipality that need to be carried out and improved. I would like to take this opportunity to talk to you about them. First, Qingdao's finances are currently in deficit. This phenomenon must be remedied. It has now been decided to cut redundant agencies and overstaffed personnel to ensure that expenditures are within the limits of income, so as not to waste public funds. The second is construction. Qingdao was just a barren peninsula thirty years ago, and it was only through the efforts of foreigners that it developed to its current state. Since our country took over, it has gradually declined, which is very bad. In the future, we will actively engage in construction, such as expanding waterworks and building more docks. At present, the Central Government is in extreme financial difficulty. If we want to take money from the Central Government to expand Qingdao's construction, it is impossible. I will only use Qingdao's income in Qingdao and not divert it to other uses. The third is culture and sports. Although Qingdao's material construction and industry and commerce are developed, and the population has increased to more than 300,000, culture and sports are very backward and undeveloped. As far as schools are concerned, there are too few. In the future, we will pay special attention to promoting culture and sports to promote their advancement. The fourth is labor and labor unrest. Before I came, I knew that Qingdao's labor unrest was very turbulent last year. After arriving in Qingdao, I have been talking to the Municipal Party Department about labor issues for days, and four methods have been agreed upon: (1) If workers have demands on the capitalists, the Municipal Government and the Party Department will negotiate with the factory on their behalf, except for minor matters. (2) The occurrence of strikes in factories is very bad. The Municipal Government and the Party Department will jointly inform all workers that they must not strike in the future and must work hard. (3) The government will provide appropriate placement for unemployed workers who are good. (4) Bad workers will be punished according to the law. Finally, I would like to ask you to give your advice from time to time. If there is anything wrong, please feel free to criticize and correct it." At this point, it was already after 6:00 PM, so tea and refreshments were served and the meeting adjourned.

Overview of Qingdao's Construction 57

Qingdao's construction industry is based on the legacy of the German and Japanese operations. It should have considerable achievements. However, from the time of takeover to the present, not only has there been no progress, but even maintaining the status quo has been declining due to financial constraints. The following is a report on the construction of Qingdao's waterworks, forestry, and road engineering in recent years, based on investigations:

(1) Waterworks: After the Germans leased Qingdao in 1898, they began to operate the waterworks. The Japanese continued to develop water sources and install water pipes when they took over Qingdao. By the time China took over, there were three water sources: (1) Licun water source, which can produce more than 6,000 tons of water per day; (2) Baisha River water source, which can produce more than 6,000 tons of water per day; and (3) Haibo River water source, which can produce 900 tons of water per day. The water pipes are installed throughout the city, and water can flow to Cangku and Sifang, making it very convenient for citizens to use water. In recent years, the population has increased, and the Municipal Government has opened a new water source downstream of the Baisha River, which is currently installing machinery. It is expected that it can produce 3,000 tons of water per day, so there will be no water shortage even during the spring drought. However, the waterworks machinery installed by the Germans has been in use for more than 30 years. The lifespan of the water pipes is only 13 years, and the lifespan of the machinery at the water source is only 4 years. Now, for the sake of preparedness, we should try to reserve funds for the replacement of new pipes and machinery. In 1927, it was proposed to save 251,100 yuan per year for the replacement of new pipes, but it failed to materialize due to insufficient funds. It is reported that the replacement of German-made machinery and water pipes requires a total of 1.4 million yuan, and the replacement of Japanese-made machinery and water pipes requires 1.85 million yuan.

(2) Forestry: Qingdao, with its barren mountains, was transformed into lush greenery through the German's full-scale afforestation efforts, making it famous for its beautiful scenery. The Germans invested 152 million German marks in Qingdao's forestry, with 37,300 acres of official forest, 350 acres of farmland, 16 parks, and 5,900 acres of private forest. The arrangement and planting of forests can truly be a model for the whole country. During the Japanese occupation, more than 300,000 Japanese yen were allocated annually to continue the expansion, which was still progressive. Since our country took over, it has only been able to maintain the status quo due to financial constraints, and the annual expenditure on agriculture and forestry is only more than 59,000 yuan. Therefore, although the Agricultural and Forestry Office has repeatedly had expansion plans, it has failed to materialize. It is reported that the office plans to afforest 150 acres in Laoshan this year and will add 30 acres on the anniversary of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's death to promote afforestation.

(3) Road Engineering: Qingdao's road engineering is very advanced, and the roads in the city are especially neat and clean. Currently, there are approximately more than 300 li of roads in the city, totaling 1.8 million square meters, of which 330,000 square meters are asphalt roads. The roads outside the city leading to Laoshan, Licun, Shazikou, Cangku and other places are also more than 300 Chinese li, totaling 870,000 square meters. Since the takeover, 140,000 square meters of new asphalt roads and more than 10,000 square meters of gravel roads have been built. The annual maintenance cost of road engineering is about 120,000 yuan. Qingdao's construction industry is relatively successful in this area, and the addition of roads in remote areas is also being planned.

Survey of Women's Occupations in Jinan 58

Jinan Correspondence: Since the success of the revolution and the emancipation of women, the number of women with jobs has gradually increased, even in Jinan. Many women are working in Party affairs, and women are also gradually appearing in administrative offices. Among them, the increase in the education sector is particularly obvious. Due to various reasons, the status of women's occupations in industry, commerce, and other classes has not progressed. The following is a record of the number of women in various fields and the comparison with the number of men, based on the survey:

Administrative Agencies: Provincial Government: 131 men, 8 women; Department of Civil Affairs: 94 men, 0 women; Department of Finance: 115 men, 0 women; Department of Construction: 70 men, 0 women; Department of Education: 35 men, 1 woman; Department of Agriculture and Mining: 40 men, 0 women; Department of Industry and Commerce: 41 men, 0 women; Municipal Government: 43 men, 2 women; Municipal Finance Bureau: 41 men, 0 women; Municipal Social Affairs Bureau: 37 men, 0 women; Municipal Public Works Bureau: 40 men, 0 women; Municipal Public Security Bureau: 88 men, 0 women; River Affairs Bureau: 53 men, 0 women;

Party Affairs Agencies: Provincial Party Department: 60 men, 7 women; Provincial Women's Association: 11 women; Municipal Party Department: 25 men, 0 women; County Party Department: 23 men, 1 woman; County Women's Association: 4 women;

Education: Senior High School: 36 men, 5 women; First Middle School: 36 men, 1 woman; Girls' Middle School: 11 men, 4 women; First Vocational School: 26 men, 0 women; Girls' Vocational School: 15 men, 3 women; First Normal School: 46 men, 0 women; Girls' Normal School: 15 men, 12 women; Mass Education Center: 37 men, 9 women; First Experimental Elementary School: 15 men, 10 women; Second Experimental Elementary School: 22 men, 6 women; Third Experimental Elementary School: 9 men, 22 women; Fourth Experimental Elementary School: 13 men, 8 women; Fifth Experimental Elementary School: 10 men, 7 women; (The above is based on the statistics of staff and teachers in various schools in the second half of the 18th year of the Department of Education.) Girls' Normal School Affiliated Elementary School: 8 men, 13 women; First Normal School Affiliated Elementary School 1: 11 men, 11 women; First Normal School Affiliated Elementary School 2: 6 men, 4 women; Beiyuan Normal School: 9 men, 0 women; Rural First Normal School: 14 men, 0 women; Rural Normal School Center Elementary School: 5 men, 1 woman; Zhengyi Middle School: 30 men, 1 woman; Zhengyi Affiliated Elementary School 1: 7 men, 2 women; Zhengyi Affiliated Elementary School 2: 4 men, 1 woman;

Business: There are the fewest women in the Jinan business community. Those completely operated by women include the Girls' Commercial Firm on Xiaowei Liu Road and the Girls' Photography Studio, but they are very small in scale. There are also not many female employees in other stores, only in a few places such as the Yinguang Theater.

Industry: Larger factories in Jinan that are easy to investigate include: Lufeng Yarn Factory, with more than 1,200 female workers; Zhengye Match Factory, with more than 200 female workers; Dongyulong Tobacco Factory, with 50 female workers; Tailong Foreign Firm Hairnet Factory, with 600 female workers. Other small hairnet factories, hat factories, and household women's handicrafts, such as pasting matchboxes, are difficult to count at once, but are estimated to be only more than 1,000 people.

Hospitals: There are only one or two female doctors in Jinan. There are also not many female nurses in hospitals. The Republican Hospital has about 30 people, the Jinan Hospital has 8 people, and the Wanda Hospital, Dehua Hospital, and Sanmin Hospital each have only one or two people.

According to the population statistics of the Jinan Public Security Bureau, there are more than 250,000 men and more than 150,000 women. The difference between men and women is as many as 100,000 people, and only a few thousand of these 150,000 women are employed. Nine out of ten are buried in the family. This is because the organization of Chinese cities is centered on men. This is something that those who are enthusiastic about the women's movement should pay attention to.

Plan for Reorganizing the Local Defense Forces in Hunan Province 59

And Conducting a Census

Changsha Correspondence: The Hunan Provincial Government, in order to make the organization of local defense forces in various counties sound so that bandits and communists have no way to use their skills and to facilitate the local suppression of bandits and communists, has decided to strictly reorganize the local defense forces. The province's 76 counties will be divided into 22 districts, each with a commander who has been appointed separately to supervise the training effectively. In order to facilitate the progress and to achieve perfection, a committee for reorganizing the local defense forces and a committee for conducting a census have been organized. Liu Qingchu, Chen Xiangwan, Cheng Jian, He Zhichao, Yi Jiawei, Li Qiong, Li Chengen, Wu Xun, Wu Xun, Yang Hua, and Xie Liangyu have been hired as members of the two committees. The regulations for the organization of the two committees have been promulgated and implemented according to the established methods for reorganizing the local defense forces and conducting a census. The regulations are recorded below.

Regulations for the Local Defense Forces Committee: (Article 1) The purpose of this committee is to promote the perfect handling of local defense forces throughout the province. (Article 2) This committee is organized by the following personnel, with a quota of 13 to 15 people: (1) Chief of Staff and chiefs of various departments of the headquarters, chief of the Second Section of the General Staff Department; (2) Advisors to the headquarters; (3) Personnel specially designated by the commander. (Article 3) The meeting of this committee will review the following matters: (1) Organization of the seal; (2) Training of the local defense forces; (3) Equipment and funding of the local defense forces; (4) Awards, punishments, and pensions for the local defense forces; (5) Dispatching personnel to various counties to reorganize the local defense forces; (6) Other matters that need to be improved; (7) Matters specially referred by the commander for discussion. (Article 4) For matters that need to be discussed with the Department of Civil Affairs, the Department of Civil Affairs may be requested to send personnel to the meeting at any time by letter from this committee. (Article 5) The Chief of Staff will be the chairman of the meeting. If the Chief of Staff is unable to attend due to business, a chairman may be temporarily appointed. (Article 6) Every Wednesday at 2:00 PM is the regular meeting of this committee. If there are special matters, a meeting may be convened temporarily. (Article 7) The standard for resolutions in the meeting is that more than half of the committee members present must pass the resolution. (Article 8) During the meeting, the General Staff Department of the headquarters will send a clerk to record the matters discussed and to preserve the files. (Article 9) All resolutions will be reported to the commander for approval and then handed over to the person in charge for execution. (Article 10) This committee will not receive additional funding. (Article 11) This regulation may be amended at any time if there are any matters that have not been fully covered. (Article 12) This regulation shall be implemented after being approved by the commander.

Regulations for the Census Committee: (Article 1) The purpose of this committee is to effectively supervise the census in various counties and to handle it perfectly. (Article 2) This committee is organized by the following personnel, with a quota of 13 to 15 people: (1) Chief of Staff and chiefs of various departments of the headquarters; (2) Advisors to the headquarters; (3) Personnel specially designated by the commander. (Article 3) The meeting of this committee will review the following matters: (1) Reviewing the master registers that have been sent. If there are errors in various counties; (2) Urging counties that have not sent the master registers to expedite the creation and submission of them; (3) Matters that should be improved in the census in various counties; (4) Examining the handling of joint guarantee matters in various counties; (5) Examining the supervision of self-reform and surrender matters in various counties; (6) Matters specially referred by the commander for discussion. (Article 4) For matters that need to be discussed with the Department of Civil Affairs, the Department of Civil Affairs may be requested to send personnel to the meeting at any time by letter from this committee. (Article 5) The Chief of Staff of the headquarters will be the chairman of the meeting. If the Chief of Staff is unable to attend due to business, a chairman may be temporarily appointed. (Article 6) This committee will hold a regular meeting every Friday at 2:00 PM, but temporary meetings may be convened in case of special events. (Article 7) The standard for resolutions in the meeting is that more than half of the committee members present must pass the resolution. (Article 8) During the meeting, an advisor from the headquarters will send a clerk to record the matters discussed and to keep the files. (Article 9) All resolutions will be reported to the commander for approval and issued to the person in charge for execution. (Article 10) This committee will not receive additional funding. (Article 11) This regulation may be amended at any time if there are any matters that have not been fully covered. (Article 12) This regulation shall be implemented after being approved by the commander.

Japanese Postal Service in South Manchuria 60

Shenyang Correspondence: Among the Japanese economic aggressions, the South Manchurian postal service has nearly 200 general bureaus, branch bureaus, and agency offices established in the three northeastern provinces. The airmail service has also achieved considerable results, with annual revenue of more than 6 million. In addition, telegraph and telephone lines and radio waves are like a net that surrounds and covers the southern part of Northeast China. The investigation is as follows:

History and Evolution: The Japanese postal rights in our Northeast have no basis in treaty and have not been recognized by us. They were obtained entirely by plunder. Initially, during the Russo-Japanese War, 94 military post offices were established as military communication agencies. After the war, they took advantage of the situation to expand, and in 1906 (the 22nd year of the reign of Emperor Guangxu of the Qing Dynasty), all military post offices were transferred to the jurisdiction of the Kwantung Government-General. From then on, it was completely organized as a postal service, and postal and telegraph offices were established to manage it. After the necessary reorganization, there were 36 post offices and 8 branch offices at that time. Afterwards, they were added year by year. By the 9th year of the Taisho era, there were more than 200 post offices, branch offices, and agency offices. In that year, a major reform of the postal system was carried out, and the Postal and Telegraph Office was renamed the Communications Management Bureau. All telegrams, telephones, radio, and airmail services were placed under its

Page 16

management.

Expansion over the Years: Since the Japanese seized our postal rights out of thin air, they have been actively expanding them several times, making steady progress and sparing no effort. After the Pacific Conference, all countries withdrew their post offices in China, but Japan still stubbornly maintained its postal service in the Northeast and refused to return it, because it had already tasted great benefits and would not give up halfway. The following is a table showing the postal progress over the years:

Increase in the Number of Ordinary Postal Items

The volume of mail listed in the table above, except for Showa 1, where regular mail and parcels suddenly decreased, has increased in all other years. The magnitude of this increase is truly astonishing. In contrast, our country's postal service is showing signs of decline everywhere. According to the Shenyang Postal Workers' Union, "In recent years, our country's postal service has not only made no progress, but has also shown a tendency to shrink. For example, the length of postal routes has now been reduced by more than 13,000 li..." This situation, compared to the postal service operated by Japan in our Northeast, is truly concerning.

Current Situation: Since the reform in Taisho 9 (1920), the postal service has developed rapidly, with increasing establishments each year. To date, there are more than 200 Japanese postal institutions in southern Manchuria. The frequency of increases and the current numbers are listed below:

Year | Post Offices | Postal Branch Offices | Postal Agencies | Postal Commissioned Agencies

Meiji 39 (1906) | 36 | 8

Taisho 1 (1912) | 30 | 14 | 10 | 70

Taisho 5 (1916) | 30 | 16 | 10 | 74

Taisho 10 (1921) | 42 | 13 | 6 | 75

Showa 1 (1926) | 40 | 8 | 16 | 146

Showa 2 (1927) | 41 | 8 | 17 | 159

Showa 3 (1928) | 42 | 9 | 18 | 40

The figures listed above are as of the end of Showa 3 (1928). (The 17th year of the Republic of China) There were already 218 post offices, branch offices, commissioned agencies, etc. The number of establishments increased in the past two years are not included in these figures. The post offices are mostly located in larger towns, followed by branch offices and postal agencies. As for the commissioned agencies, they are set up at small stations along the railway lines and in various villages and settlements within the Japanese leased territories. The locations are listed below:

Along the South Manchuria Railway: Lushun, Dalian, Xiaogangzi, Shahekou, Yingshu, Piziwo, Jinzhou, Pulandian, Wafangdian, Xiongyue, Gaiping, Dashiqiao, Haicheng, Qianshan, Anshan, Lishan, Shoushan, Liaoyang, Yantai, Sujiatun, Shenyang, Fushun, Xintaizi, Tieling, Kaiyuan, Changtu, Shuangmiaozi, Sipingjie, Guojiadian, Gongzhuling, Fanjiatun, Changchun, Andong Line: Andong, Dadonggou, Fenghuangcheng, Qiaotou, Caohekou, Lianshanguan, Benxi, Yanji, Longjingcun, Xinmin.

Among the post offices listed above, Andong, Changchun, Shenyang, Liaoyang, Yingkou, Tieling, Dalian, and Sipingjie are eight exchange offices that exchange mail with our country's post offices. Among them, the busiest post offices along the railway line, in addition to Changchun and Shenyang, are Fushun, Anshan, Kaiyuan, Yapingjie, Benxi, and Liaoyang. On average, each receives and sends 110,000 to 140,000 pieces of regular mail daily, and 500 to 1,100 parcels. The amount of postal savings is also considerable. In Showa 3, the total savings of Japanese people in the Northeast amounted to more than 18.9 million yuan. In Showa 4, it is said to have exceeded 20 million yuan, an increase of more than 12 million yuan, which is a huge sum.

Airmail: The Japanese Aviation Law was promulgated in June of Showa 2 (1927). In August of the same year, an imperial ordinance was issued to apply the law to the leased territory of Kwantung. Therefore, the experimental flight of the Japan Aviation Company in September of Taisho 15 (1926) was revived, and there was an air transport plan between Dalian and Japan. In Showa 4 (1929), with government subsidies, the Japan Air Transport Company established flights on the Dalian-Tokyo route, implementing the transportation of mail, goods, and passengers between Dalian, Pyongyang, Keijo (Seoul), Ulsan, Okayama, Osaka, and Tokyo. However, goods such as alcohol, tobacco, textiles, corrosives, and flammable materials were not accepted for transportation. The volume of goods was limited to no more than 2.3 Japanese feet in length, and no more than 1.3 Japanese feet in width and thickness. The frequency of flights and postage rates are listed below:

Tokyo-Dalian Route

Round Trip Weekly | Round Trip Weekly

Tokyo-Osaka: 1-2 times | Osaka-Fukuoka: 6 times

Fukuoka-Keijo: 6 times | Keijo-Dalian: 6 times

Postage Rates | Dalian-Korea | Dalian-Korea-Japan

Sealed Letter (weight limit 4 taels) | 18 sen | 33 sen

Unsealed Letter (weight limit 10 taels) | 17 sen | 33 sen

Postcard | 8.5 sen | 16.5 sen

Parcel (limit 200 taels) | 1 yuan 12 sen

Registered Parcel (same limit) | 1 yuan 12 sen | 2 yuan 45 sen

Note: For express mail sent from Tokyo, Yokohama, Osaka, Kyoto, Kobe, Keijo, etc., an additional 8 sen postage is required.

Although airmail has been in operation for less than a year, and there are no reliable statistics on its transportation volume, it appears from the surface that the transportation of goods and letters is very active. It is said that newspapers sent from Osaka can reach Harbin in three days, and the same is true for letters. Our country's newspapers from Tianjin and Beijing are lagging behind. The current Liaoning authorities plan to open an air transport service with 20 airplanes. If this can be realized, it will be a somewhat encouraging event.

Local News

Jiading 62

Rogue Extortion Leads to Discovery of Opium: A man named Jia from Zhaotun Bridge in Qingpu, nearly 50 years old, and a young woman, returned from Shanghai on the 11th of this month. They got off the Beijing-Shanghai train at Anting Station, carried their belongings, and walked home. When they passed the Caotang Village area, they were spotted by local rogues Shao Abing, Agen, and others, who suspected them of abduction. They were intercepted and questioned, and more than ten packs of opium, of considerable value, were found in their luggage. Shao and others threatened them extremely, intending to embezzle the opium. Jia's attempt to bribe them was unsuccessful. Then, a man named Ding intervened and persuaded them to divide the opium equally, and hired a boat for Jia to send him back. Unexpectedly, Shao and others started a fight over the division, which was heard by the local policeman Gu Fushan, who reported it to the Eighth District Office for thorough investigation and punishment.

Impersonating Representatives Exposed on the Spot: In Anting Town, of this county, two men named Zhang Shusheng and Xu Weikang, claiming to be representatives of refugees from Zhangde, Henan, and carrying a passport issued by the Public Security Bureau of that county, requested repatriation from the District Office on the 13th of this month. When District Head Qian asked about the number of people, they replied that there were more than 300 people stationed in the Baihejiang Temple. Qian suspected that most of these representatives were impersonating, and that the Public Security Bureau had issued an order to investigate, detain, and send them. He instructed Zhang and Xu to wait temporarily, and sent Chen Yusheng, the squad leader of the security corps, to investigate, but found no trace of them. It was clear that they were impersonating for fraud. He ordered Chen to bring them back and detain them, and prepared a document to send them for handling. Zhang and Xu, realizing that they had been exposed, prostrated themselves and begged for mercy. Qian then rebuked them and sent them away.

Fengxian 63

Record of Interrogation After the Capture of Bandits: Yang Chasheng, the head of the second police detachment of Zhuangxing, previously cracked the bandit den at Daijia Bridge and had already transferred the three bandit leaders to the county government. Yesterday afternoon, County Magistrate Hong interrogated them. Chen Shusan (also known as Bái Tóu (White Head)), confessed that he lived in the eleventh ward of Songjiang County. On the 24th night of the lunar new year, his accomplices from Shanghai, Li Tingyang, Li Guijie, Yang Xiaoli, Gu Xingcai, Luo Jincai, and Wu Ati, an unknown man from Shanghai, totaled twelve people. They carried several Mauser pistols and gathered at the Tang residence every night at 9 o'clock. They successively led the gang to rob fourteen families, including Zhang Huan's. Chen Shusan would act as lookout with a carrying pole. Afterwards, the Li surname would distribute the loot. Since he didn't know how to use a gun, he only got twelve thousand copper coins and a quilted blanket. He originally had two blankets, but his eldest son, Agen, had been assassinated last autumn. Dai Xiaocai confessed that he was also an accomplice of Li and others. During this robbery, there were also Chen Ad, Tang Huanxiang, Zhang Meitou and several others. The loot was divided into thirteen shares by the Li surname at Chen Shusan's house. They robbed gold rings, gold hairpins, pearl circles, silver coins, banknotes, woolen cloth, clothes, salted chicken, and cured pork legs, totaling more than two hundred items. The Li surname transported all of them to Shanghai. Another bandit gave a similar confession. County Magistrate Hong considers the Tang and Li gangs to be well-known communists and that they are also related to the arson case in Zhuangxing. Therefore, in addition to ordering their detention for further investigation, he also ordered that they be wanted within a time limit and brought to justice.

Formal Commencement of Land Registration: The Finance Bureau, upon receiving orders to handle land registration, submitted a report on the 10th of this month to commence operations and set up a sub-office within the Eighth District Office. It also ordered the land stewards of each district to inform the landowners to apply for registration within one month. All regulations were specially printed and distributed by the bureau yesterday for reference.

Suzhou 64

Higher Court Sets Deadline for Concluding Unresolved Cases: Lin Biao, President of the Jiangsu Higher Court, stated that the number of prisoners in various counties is congested. The prisoner's food is not only insufficient, but also the health of the prisoners is a concern during this warmer weather. Therefore, yesterday (the 15th), he ordered the county magistrates and trial officers to expedite the conclusion of unresolved cases to reduce the number of prisoners. He also established several methods to reduce the number of prisoners to be followed and implemented. He ordered the conclusion of cases within one month, with the following methods: (1) Criminal defendants should strictly adhere to Article 66 of the Criminal Procedure Law, and may not be detained unless they meet the conditions of Articles 41 to 43 of the same law. (2) If the defendant is charged with a crime punishable by detention or a fine, they should be released on bail immediately and not detained. (3) If the criminal defendant has been detained in the county for more than two months, they should cite Article 14 of the Provisional Regulations for the Trial of Lawsuits by Amended County Magistrates, state the reasons, and submit them to the court for a ruling; otherwise, they should be released immediately. (4) When the cause of detention ceases, they should be released immediately or released on bail in accordance with Article 72 of the Criminal Procedure Law. (5) For unresolved detainees, those with lighter suspicions and no need for detention should be released on bail in accordance with Articles 75 to 80 of the Criminal Procedure Law, and the following measures should be implemented: (A) Order the payment of a reasonable guarantee deposit, securities, or the issuance of a store guarantee letter for release on bail. (B) Entrust to relatives or other appropriate persons. (C) Restrict the defendant's residence. (6) Defendants sentenced to detention for a term of imprisonment of two years or less, who meet the conditions for probation, should be granted probation in accordance with Article 90 of the Criminal Law. (7) If the Criminal Law stipulates a fine, imprisonment, or detention, and allows for the selection of one, the fine should be imposed after considering the circumstances.

Jiangning Court Prosecutor Accused: Zhou, a prosecutor at the Jiangning District Court, was accused by Zhou Daihuang and several other county residents of Jiangning County in a document submitted to the High Court. They stated that he was unfair in handling cases and abused his power to detain people illegally. They requested that personnel be dispatched to investigate the matter in detail. After receiving the report, Court President Lin decided to send personnel on the 17th to investigate the matter thoroughly and then determine the appropriate course of action.

Bandits from Banghu Return to Suzhou Territory: The Wu County Government received a telegram from Kunshan County yesterday (the 15th), stating that a large gang of lake bandits, estimated at more than 700 people, had infiltrated into the Jiaozhi area from Chenmu Township yesterday morning. After Huang County Magistrate approved the telegram, he immediately ordered the Fourth Branch of the Kunshan County Public Security Bureau to take appropriate precautions, and ordered the police team to intercept them. He also telegraphed the Third District of the Water Police, requesting that teams eleven and twelve and the guerrillas be dispatched to jointly suppress them.

Wuxi 65

The Urgent Need to Eliminate Lake Bandits: The Taihu Lake basin is a crucial area. Since recently, lake bandits have been rampant, with the Longwang Temple in Wujiang being looted. The Shanghai-Changshu passenger ship has been robbed four times in a week. In addition, small passenger ships and villages and towns along the lake in Pingwang (Suzhou), Jiaxing, and other places have been harassed. This not only disrupts public order but also hinders waterway transportation. Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek issued a telegram on New Year's Day, ordering General Commander Hu to quickly lead his troops stationed in Suzhou and Wuxi to suppress the bandits immediately according to the original plan. General Commander Hu, upon receiving the telegram, dispatched the 25th Regiment of his troops from their defense area in Suqian to Suzhou the day before yesterday. The heads of the various departments of the regimental headquarters and the artillery battalion arrived in Wuxi yesterday (the 15th). The 30th Regiment of the brigade also arrived in Songjiang at the same time. The 28th Regiment is also scheduled to be stationed in the lakeside area of Wuxi within the next few days. Once the anti-bandit troops from all directions have completed their deployment, they will join forces with the police forces from Suzhou and Zhejiang to suppress the bandits on land and water on a selected date.

Nunnery Robbed: The Jingtu Nunnery, near Xialian Bridge in Hongshengli, Nanyan Township of this county, is usually quite popular with worshippers. It houses more than ten nuns, young and old. At around one o'clock the night before last, eight or nine male and female bandits suddenly arrived, wielding knives, sticks, flashlights, and other weapons. They broke open the nunnery gate and rushed in, tying up the nuns with ropes, beating them severely. Then, they overturned boxes and chests, searching extensively. After an hour, they escaped with their loot. After the incident, an inspection revealed that they had stolen silver coins, clothing, rice, and other items, causing a total loss of more than one hundred yuan.

Communist Murders Villager in Tianshang Market: Chen Jida, a villager from Chenxiang Shangxiang near Zhang Village in Tianshang Market, makes a living as a farmer. He has a modest household. However, because Chen Jida had always been strongly anti-communist, the communists in the village harbored deep resentment. At around one o'clock in the afternoon the day before yesterday, Chen was shopping on Zhang Village Street when he was unexpectedly ambushed by two communists, You and Cao, who grabbed him and stabbed him four times in the right leg with a sharp knife. Blood flowed freely, and he rolled around in agony. The two bandits, You and Cao, then left. Chen cried out for help, and someone ran to inform his family. Chen's mother, upon hearing the news, rushed to the scene, first helped her son home, called a doctor to treat him, and then went to the public security sub-bureau to request a manhunt.

Tragic Murder Case Occurs at Huangbudun: Wu, a resident of house number 10 near Huangbudun, outside the North Gate of this county, was from Zhenjiang, aged 47. Her husband, Jia Liansheng, died of illness two years ago. Unable to sleep alone, Wu remarried Chen Shunchang, a boatman of the seventh patrol boat of the first detachment of the sixth team of the water police, and took in a girl named Aidi (8 years old) as an adopted daughter. Unexpectedly, last night, Wu was suddenly killed with a knife, her head severed from her body, a gruesome sight. The local land steward and the family members of the deceased reported the case to the county government for an autopsy. It is said that the cause of Wu's murder was likely due to an affair.

Changzhou 66

The 28th Regiment of the Fifth Division Arrives in Changzhou: The 28th Regiment of the 14th Brigade of the Fifth Division of the Army was ordered to station three battalions of its troops in Changzhou. The entire regiment of officers and soldiers arrived in Changzhou at 7:00 PM on the 14th and are reportedly stationed at Taiping Temple, Tianning Temple, and Qingliang Temple.

Dispatching Personnel to Supervise the Distribution of Pensions: The village of Xueyanqiao in Wu County was previously looted by lake bandits, and the county had submitted a request for pensions. The Finance Department has now issued a payment order, instructing the Finance Bureau to allocate 1,500 yuan for distribution. The County Government has been instructed to dispatch Assistant Rui Guangxiu to supervise the distribution and order the director of the eighth district to collect the funds from the government, handle the matter jointly, and report back.

Changshu 67

Dispute Among Doctors After Cai's Autopsy: The body of Cai Lianbao, the adopted daughter-in-law of Liu Tonghuai of Shanxiang Lane in the city, was autopsied by Chen, a trial officer of the county government, along with ten Western doctors, including Gu Yuanhao, Zhou Guanwen, Gu Jianshan, Zhou Mansun, Zhou Tianmai, Shao Yufan, Xie Tang, Wu Juncheng, and Gu Zhihe. The next day, Xie Tang sent the autopsy record to the doctors present for signature. Unexpectedly, Gu Yuanhao, a doctor at Jishan Hospital, refused to sign, citing three reasons: (1) He had never heard of using concentrated nitric acid to test gastric fluid. (2) He had doubts about the cut duodenum, fearing that the part cut was actually the small intestine. (3) The brain and spinal cord he had extracted were still being cultured and had not yet been tested. He also claimed that the nine people present did not express any concerns at the time, so he did not raise any objections. If the part cut was indeed the small intestine and not the duodenum, would he not be laughed at if he signed the document? The nine doctors who had signed the document learned of this and held a meeting of the Medical Association at the First District Office on the 13th to discuss countermeasures. As a result, they raised four questions for Gu Yuanhao and sent a letter to Gu requesting a response: (1) According to the doctors present during the autopsy, Zhou Mansheng and Gu Jianshan, the section of the duodenum (approximately three inches) that was cut was approximately three inches from the stomach, close to the jejunum. (Since the duodenum is approximately ten inches long, the section cut should undoubtedly be the duodenum. If the bile duct opening was not retained, it should be clarified. This is the first question to be addressed.) (2) Testing the stomach contents is a research-oriented matter, and it was stated at the time that it would not be used as evidence. Therefore, there is no report in the expert opinion. It is thought that your hospital has considerable experience in testing opium addicts and has accurate methods for detecting opium reactions. This is the second question to be addressed. (3) Before the autopsy, there was a meeting at the county government where it was decided that only the stomach, intestines, liver, lungs, heart, urine, and stomach contents needed to be taken. You were also present and agreed. If you believed that it was necessary to extract the bladder and uterus for testing, why did you not state so at the time? This is the third question to be addressed. (4) The county government summoned the doctors to the autopsy site to gather ideas and benefit from everyone's wisdom. You were also present. If you believed that the procedures were not in accordance with regulations, why did you not provide guidance at the time? Why did you refuse to sign the document afterwards? What exactly was your intention? These are the four questions listed for clarification. As for the county government, it extracted the stomach contents, lungs, liver, heart, intestines, and other vital parts from Lianbao's body, along with urine, sealed them in bottles, and sent them by police on the early morning Suzhou boat to the Prosecutor's Office of the High Court on the morning of the 14th to request a designated hospital to test for toxic substances for further investigation.

Electricity Bill Issue Resolved: The Electric Utility Users Association and the Electric Utility Company had been in dispute over improving treatment and electricity bills for a long time and had not yet resolved the issue. At noon on the 12th, six representatives of the Electric Utility Users Association, along with mediators Xiang Juecheng and Gui Junan, and Electric Utility Company manager Yu Qihan and director Zhou Jiongru, met at the New Hotel to discuss the matter for a long time. The Association insisted on an electricity rate of 26 cents per kilowatt-hour, while the Company insisted on 28 cents. The mediators attempted to mediate at 27 cents, but it was unsuccessful. They then attempted to mediate at 27.5 cents, but the Electric Utility Company insisted on 27.8 cents, and the discussion was suspended. On the afternoon of the 13th, the three parties met again at Yao's residence in Jicui Garden, and finally reached an agreement at 27.6 cents. The Electric Utility Company and the Electric Utility Users Association signed an agreement with eight clauses, each holding a copy, and submitted them to the county for record.

Provincial and County Police Teams Search Bandit Areas: Bandits are rampant in the Yudong Sanyi and other districts. Provincial and county police teams went to jointly suppress them. On the 13th, they encountered a group of three to four hundred bandits northeast of Touqiao and engaged in a fierce battle for two hours, killing more than ten bandits. On the 14th, the police team searched the bandit areas and pursued the routed bandits.

Thorough Investigation of Police Extortion Case: Xu Shifa, the Director of the Nantong County Public Security Bureau, sent police officers to the Xiehecheng Xiyan Inn to search for opium but found none. They extorted 1,000 yuan. This matter shocked the entire county. Zhao Dongchen, the victim, submitted a petition to the county government for a thorough investigation. On the 14th, the county magistrate approved the petition, instructing the bureau director to remove the officers involved from their positions, recover the extorted money, return it to the owner, and severely punish them. The petition also noted that the government should not condone such actions to avoid similar incidents.

Fundraising for the Merchant Corps: The Nantong-Chongming-Haimen-Taixing General Chamber of Commerce has a Merchant Corps expense of 1,092 yuan per month, which has always been offset by merchant donations. However, recently, donations have been short. The Standing Committee has decided to relaunch a fundraising campaign, and has designated members to take responsibility for soliciting donations.

Zhenjiang 69

Urging the Delivery of Disbandment Treasury Bonds: The Jiangsu Provincial Association for Soliciting Disbandment Treasury Bonds stated that the quota for bonds solicited by the branches in various counties had long passed its deadline, and the number of bonds verified and delivered was mostly insufficient. Therefore, yesterday, it urgently urged the members of the branches in various counties to redouble their efforts to solicit the full amount of bonds and deliver them to the treasury as soon as possible, obtain receipts for verification and registration, and then submit them for assessment and evaluation for rewards and punishments.

Reorganizing the Police Forces of Five Counties: The Department of Civil Affairs stated that the police forces of Nantong, Rugao, Taixing, Taixian, and Jingjiang counties were ineffective in suppressing bandits and had been negligent in their organization, which was insufficient to defend against banditry. Therefore, yesterday, it specially ordered Li Changjiang, the Captain of the Jiangsu Provincial Police Corps, to immediately go to the counties to work with the county magistrates to effectively reorganize the police forces. Li Changjiang was also ordered to report the reorganization status at any time. Furthermore, Director Miao of the Department of Civil Affairs stated that banditry was rampant in various counties of Jiangsu Province recently, and the provincial police force was insufficient to handle the situation. He specially ordered Captain Li to immediately recruit 500 provincial police officers and send them to Zhenjiang for training as soon as possible to defend against and suppress bandits and communists.

Resignation of the Director of the Relief Home Not Approved: The Provincial Relief Home was established in June of last year. Since then, it has taken over four institutions. Under the hard work of Director Yu, it has achieved considerable success. It is now reported that Director Yu Youren has submitted his resignation because the home's funding has been repeatedly reduced, making it difficult to implement various plans. The department has persuaded him to stay. Currently, the number of people cared for in the various institutions is gradually increasing, while the price of rice is high. The original funding is insufficient to cover expenses, and educational aspects cannot be implemented as desired. Therefore, he has repeatedly requested to resign.

The Bandit Leader Cai Hanyu at the Time of Execution: Cai Hanyu (also known as Cai Laowu), the leader of the Liyang riot (i.e., the leader of the Big Sword Society), was captured in Shanghai. The Zhenjiang Jiangsu Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, upon receiving an order from the department, welcomed him and brought him to Zhenjiang. At 3:00 PM today, it received a telegram from the provincial government ordering the execution by shooting. The bandit, currently 41 years old, was wearing a Serge mandarin jacket and a thread-spring sheepskin robe. His demeanor was calm at the time of execution, and he requested three conditions: (1) Purchase a coffin for burial. (2) Do not refer to him as a bandit leader, but as a reorganization faction. (3) Everything must be treated with courtesy.

Yangzhou 70

Road Workers Assault Construction Bureau Officials: Wang Daoping, Director of the Jiangdu Construction Bureau, and two technicians, Shen and Zhou, were severely beaten by more than a thousand road workers at Huanjia Bridge on the Yanghuo Road yesterday (the 13th). The section chief's house and the policemen's guns were mostly destroyed and seized. The cause of the incident is recorded below: Yesterday morning, technician Zhou Chunfang went to inspect the Yanghuo Road line and was stopped by road workers at Huanjia Bridge, who demanded the payment of their wages. When they were refused, they beat Zhou and injured him. Wang Daoping, Director of the Bureau, and technician Shen Yuanliang, upon hearing the news, went to the location with four policemen at 2:00 PM and were also beaten and injured. The policemen tried their best to protect them and were able to escape and return. All three were sent to the hospital for treatment, and their injuries are severe. In addition, one policeman was injured, and his injuries are also not light. After the county government heard the news, it immediately sent a team to strictly arrest the ringleaders and telegraphed the Department of Construction to request instructions for handling. It is reported that the homes of the section chiefs were mostly destroyed, with Sun Xun's home being the most severely damaged. The policemen lost a Mauser pistol and a Browning pistol, as well as fifty or sixty bullets. The arrested Kang Pei is reportedly Xu Zezong's assumed name.

Meeting to Review the Budget for the Eighteenth Year: The Jiangdu County government's budget for the eighteenth year has now been compiled and sent to the government by the Finance Bureau. County Magistrate Chen scheduled a meeting in the conference room at 2:00 PM on the 15th of this month for discussion. The draft budget has been sent to various agencies and organizations for review, and all organizations are requested to send representatives to participate in the review as scheduled.

Dispute Over Boundary Lines Between District Chiefs: The second district and the tenth district of Jiangdu County are in dispute over the boundary line of Qilidian. The second district has submitted a petition to the county. It is reported that County Magistrate Chen plans to send the chief of the first district to inspect the area with the chiefs of the two districts, determine the boundary line, and submit it for approval.

Qingjiang 71

Dispute Over Field Rental of the Five Garrison Guard Areas: The hundred qing of fields in the Five Garrison Guard areas of Huai'an, since the death of the local gentry Ding Baoquan, had annual rental income of over eight thousand yuan, all going to the Huai'an Middle School and the education bureaus of Huaiyin, Lianshui, Yancheng, and Funing counties for expenditures. However, the contractor, Mou Yisan, claimed a famine in the seventeenth year of the Republic of China and petitioned the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture and Mining for a reduction in rent. The department dispatched commissioners Gao and Chen to investigate and approve the reduction. The Huai'an Middle School and the other five county education bureaus denied that this had become a reality. Mou is now suing the Huai'an County Government, requesting that it be handled as a civil lawsuit. County Magistrate Wang Guodong has already issued summons to all parties involved, ordering them to attend the court hearing (on the 24th). However, the parties involved argue that Mou's role was that of a bidder and contractor, not a direct cultivator or tenant of the educational fields. They have jointly submitted a petition to cancel the civil lawsuit and continue to handle the matter within the administrative scope, ordering Mou Yisan to pay the full amount as required without excuses.

Jingjiang 73

剿匪軍連獲三盜: The County Public Security Bureau and the County Police Team jointly went to Taixing to suppress bandits the day before yesterday, capturing Zhao Rushou, Ding Changyi, and Huang Xuekai. They were escorted to the city yesterday. After an interrogation by Judge Yin Cheng, the three bandits confessed to robbery, arson, and murder without denial. They admitted to participating in the riots in Chaijiawei, Xilaizhen and Zhoujiazhuang village last year.

Purchasing Grain to Stabilize Prices: County Magistrate Wang, concerned about the high rice prices and the difficult livelihood of the poor, has submitted a document to the Department of Civil Affairs requesting two passports to purchase 1,000 shi of rice in Shanghai and 1,000 shi of yuan wheat in Nantong, to be distributed in the countryside to stabilize prices.

Gaoyou 74

Police Officer Arrested and Escorted to the County: Song Shaosheng, a police officer from the eighth branch of the Linze Township Public Security Bureau, has a reputation for indulgence and has accomplished nothing since his arrival. The people of the town deeply resent him. The day before yesterday, he extorted farmers in connection with a certain case. Team Leader Yu of the police squad, yesterday (the 12th), specially convened the district office, district militia headquarters, and chamber of commerce to arrest Song and escort him to the city that night for handling by the county.

The Zhu Family in Zhugou Village Robbed: The home of Zhu Yongyu, a farmer in Zhugou Village, was suddenly invaded by seven or eight bandits armed with guns the night before last. They climbed over the walls, tied up Zhu and his wife, and interrogated them about the location of their silver. Hangzhou 75

Loan for Road Construction Partially Allocated: The Zhejiang Department of Finance and the Department of Construction borrowed funds from various banks and money shops for construction. Implementation of Excise Tax Abolition Should Not Be Hasty: The Zhejiang Department of Finance responded to an inquiry from the Hubei Department of Finance regarding the implementation of excise tax abolition, stating that due to the current environment, hasty action is not advisable. Therefore, the consolidated tax will temporarily remain as before, and new taxes have not yet been created. Please take note of this.

Four More Inspectors Appointed by the Department of Finance: The Zhejiang Department of Finance, having passed a resolution in the provincial government meeting, dismissed inspectors Wang Chengxiu, Li Weiming, Sun Yongshi, and Wang Zhixue, and appointed Shen Jiwei, Zheng Shiqiao, and others to replace them.

Jiashan 76

Public Security Bureau Cracks Down on Fugitive Bandit: Two travelers, a man and a woman, speaking with a Tongxiang accent, stayed at the Dongfa Inn in the county town the day before yesterday. That night, the Public Security Bureau sent Patrolman Pan to lead police officers to inspect. Seeing that the two were acting suspiciously, they questioned them. They learned that the traveler was named Shen San and the woman accompanying him was named Yan, looking distraught and speaking evasively. Patrolman Pan, suspecting their behavior, took them to the bureau for strict interrogation. Their statements were inconsistent, so they were sentenced to 15 days of detention. Unexpectedly, seven days later, the Tongxiang County Government sent a document ordering the arrest of Shen Sanbao, who had changed his surname (originally Yan). He was the main culprit in the robbery in Wuzhen in mid-November of last year. The next day, two bailiffs from the Tongxiang County Government came to the bureau to take him back for legal processing.

Public Prosecutor of the Court Transferred to Ningbo: Since the establishment of the county court in this county, all internal organization has been reorganized. Shaoxing 78

Silver and Money Industry Appeals for Reduction in Borrowing: The Shaoxing silver and money industry previously sent representative Xu Yinqiao to Hangzhou to participate in the construction bond borrowing conference. As a result, Shaoxing was assigned to subscribe for 400,000 yuan. Now, the two industries are finding it difficult to raise such a large sum. Yesterday, after public discussion, it was decided that due to the commercial depression in Shaoxing in recent years, crop failures, and an unusually depleted social finance, it is difficult to raise such a large sum. A decision was made to submit a petition to the provincial government stating the difficult situation and requesting a reduction.

Ningbo 79

Ningfeng Road Officially Opens to Traffic: The Zhejiang Provincial Highway from Ningbo to Xikou has provided convenient transportation since its opening. Recently, the main line from Jiangkou to Fenghua has also been gradually completed. Many large and small buses have been prepared, and the road is officially open to traffic on the 17th of this month. Those traveling by express bus from Ningbo to Fenghua Bridge will find that there are 14 round trips daily from 7:30 AM to 4:20 PM. Each trip takes only 28 minutes, and the ticket price is 8 jiao and 6 fen.

Ningbo Agrees to Borrow Funds for Railway Construction: The Zhejiang Provincial Government, noting that the Xiaochang Light Railway has already begun construction and urgently needs funds, convened leaders from the silver and money industry and the general chamber of commerce from Hangzhou, Jiaxing, Huzhou, Ningbo, Shaoxing, and other districts to discuss borrowing a large sum of money using construction bonds as collateral. After discussion, it was decided that the total borrowing amount for the Ningbo district would be 2.4 million yuan, with the Ningbo sub-district borrowing 400,000 yuan at a monthly interest rate of 1 fen and 2 li. The loan will be paid off in four installments, and the repayment will also be in four installments, from July to the end of October. The loan agreement is scheduled to be formally signed with the Department of Finance. Representatives Lin and Zhou returned to Ningbo yesterday to report everything to the silver and money industries.

Teachers Preparing to Demand Salary: The salaries of teachers in municipal elementary schools in Ningbo City have not been paid for two months. Teachers from various schools, concerned about their livelihood, convened a meeting yesterday and appointed Jiang Yezheng, Shen Mingluan, Wang Huai, and others to demand their salaries from the municipal government.

Robber Arrested in Pawnshop: Yang Zuquan's family in Yangjialutou Village, Naxiang, Yin County, was robbed of jewelry and clothing the day before yesterday, and his wife was injured. At 3:00 PM yesterday, the detective team arrested the robber Ye Liangsong in the Qianxun Pawnshop in Haohetou. Under questioning, Ye confessed that the leader of the robbery that day was Zhang Ashun, and he was merely accompanying him. After questioning, he was handed over to the Yin County Local Court for review.

Bandits in Upper and Lower Shamen Annihilated: Wang Xiaolan, a notorious bandit in Guankeng Village, Nanxiang, Linhai, brutally murdered soldiers of the Township Defense Corps in Nara Creek while publicly reporting on land. He then colluded with over 300 bandits from Xian County and gathered in Shangshamen, Xiashamen, Pingkeng, Guankeng, and other places in this county. Military forces once attempted to suppress them, but were unsuccessful due to the rugged terrain. Upon hearing the news, the Zhejiang Provincial Government dispatched Regiment Commander Zhu of the Fifth Regiment stationed in Jiao (Haimen, a district of Taizhou) to mobilize 700 troops with a large number of guns and cannons to encircle and suppress them. Regiment Commander Zhu personally supervised the operation, and all traces of bandits have been eliminated from Shangshamen, Xiashamen, Pingkeng, and other places. It is said that the bandits in Guankeng will be annihilated soon.

Once a large shipment of rice arrives, a bureau will be established in the city to sell it at stable prices to benefit the disaster-stricken people.
