Local News

General Post Office Savings and Remittances Bureau 82

Opening Ceremony Yesterday

The General Post Office Savings and Remittances Bureau, located at 5 Fuzhou Road, officially opened yesterday. Important figures from various sectors of the Party, government, business, and education in this city attended to offer congratulations. The gifts presented were numerous and splendid, making it a grand occasion. Minister of Communications Wang Boqun delivered a speech, followed by a response from General Manager Liu Shufan and a speech by Director-General Lin Shi of the General Post Office. The official opening was at 9:00 AM. The bureau's facilities are very well-organized, and the organization is also very perfect. It is said that the savings and remittance procedures have been substantially improved to strive for the convenience of customers. Therefore, many customers came to the bureau that day to open savings accounts, and the staff were extremely busy. To commemorate the opening, the bureau prepared wallets to distribute to new depositors. In addition, the General Bureau manages postal remittances throughout the country, so post offices everywhere are its remittance agencies. According to statistics, there are a total of 2,125 post offices nationwide, and its remittance capacity is very strong. This method of establishing a special bureau is modeled after the successful practices of various countries, and the past achievements of various countries are very impressive. Therefore, this is not only fortunate for the new business of the post office but also marks a new era for the entire postal service of our country.

Minister Wang's Address: Our country is vast and rich in resources, excelling globally, but the production industry lags behind other countries, which is due to the lack of domestic capital. The reasons for the lack of capital are threefold: (1) failure to establish national capital, (2) failure to adjust social capital, and (3) failure to concentrate individual capital. If national capital, social capital, and people's capital can be combined, various industries will surely develop. Now, during the period of political tutelage, production and beneficial industries are most important. Last year, the inspection commissioner of this department went to Europe, America, and Japan and saw that the territory and population of each country are far less than ours, but the development of the national economy is progressing rapidly. Even with postal savings and remittances, the principle of division of labor is adopted to establish special bureaus and handle matters with great care. Therefore, it complements the overall postal affairs, and its progress and development are unlimited. Therefore, integrated rules were adopted, repeatedly discussed, and approved by the National Government and the Executive Yuan, which led to the establishment of this bureau. Preparations have been underway for three months, and the opening was finally achieved. We have also received congratulations from people from all walks of life, as well as congratulatory letters and savings and remittance materials from the savings and remittance bureaus of Japan and other countries for reference, which is a great honor. Tracing back to the establishment of the postal service in our country, it has been more than 30 years. Initially, it was under the Customs, and it was not until the end of the Qing Dynasty that it separated from the Customs and became independent, which led to substantial progress. This time, the establishment of a special bureau for savings and remittances also marks a new era for the postal service. In the future, it will cooperate with the postal service and the prospects are limitless. This can be expected. Postal agencies are located everywhere, and handling savings and remittances is easy to popularize. In the future, if promotion is effective, it will arouse the savings mindset of the general public and cultivate their frugality. This can be expected in two ways. Our country's currency system has not yet been unified, and it is extremely difficult to organize finances. The postal force is scattered in various provinces, and the daily handling of currency prices and remittances in the interior of each province is clearer. Therefore, in the future, the bureau should make a great contribution to the government's work on unifying the currency system. This can be expected in three ways. The staff of this bureau are carefully selected bank experts and original postal experienced personnel. In terms of financial investment and business development, there should be more confidence, and it is expected that in the future it will be able to compete with the postal industry in Europe and the United States. This can be expected in four ways. However, it is often easy for our country to become bureaucratic. The business operation of this bureau should use scientific methods to strive for commercialization and socialization. This is what should be paid attention to most. All new businesses are created through hard work. We should have a spirit of perseverance and struggle and practice the principle of "people's livelihood first." This is what Boqun and all those involved should encourage each other to do.

General Manager Liu's Response: Today is the opening day of this bureau, and I am extremely grateful for the minister's personal instruction. I believe that the establishment of the General Post Office Savings and Remittances Bureau is extremely important. In the past, China often relied on foreign capital for every undertaking, which led to the loss of rights, increased burdens, and the national economy was on the verge of bankruptcy. However, the inherent assets of the Chinese people were deposited in foreign banks, which is regrettable. This phenomenon is due to the weakness of the people's patriotism, but also to the lack of solid institutions in our country that can make people trust, so it has come to this. The establishment of the postal service is widespread, and its nature is also extremely permanent. The earth will not be destroyed, and the postal service will surely exist. In terms of business organizations, the postal service is the most solid. If it can be guided by the situation, its progress will be unlimited. The purpose of the establishment of this bureau is roughly three things: (1) to establish a chain relationship between the people and the government. The people entrust their hard-earned assets to national institutions for safekeeping. The well-being of the country is the well-being of the people themselves. Then, all internal strife and external insults will have no place to rise. (2) To break the public's perception of trusting foreign banks. Postal guarantees have been confirmed, and the handling methods should be improved. In the future, the recovery of rights will surely be significant. (3) To gather wealth scattered throughout the country to help the development of domestic industries. All foreign capital is not used, and the benefits are immeasurable. All of this is the common goal of the national postal staff, and they must strive to achieve it in order to live up to the earnest expectations of our country and the minister.

Director-General Lin's Congratulatory Speech: Just now, I listened to the minister's instructions and General Manager Liu's response, which were very detailed about the purpose of establishing the General Post Office Savings and Remittances Bureau and the preparations. I have two impressions here: (1) The postal bureaus are located throughout the country, and now the special bureau handles savings and remittance affairs, which can concentrate national capital, generate productive enterprises, and adjust people's livelihood. It is an important construction to realize Dr. Sun Yat-sen's principle of people's livelihood. (2) It can promote the people's interest in savings and the virtue of frugality, so as to conform to the spirit of the resolution of the Third Plenary Session of the Central Committee. When the country has established a trustworthy institution, the people will dare to save with confidence. In the past, when I was in the Northwest, I personally saw the people bury silver underground, hide it in cabinets, or even spend it all. This was all because there was no reliable savings institution, which led to this. The purpose of establishing the postal savings and remittance industry is to cooperate through division of labor. Therefore, postal colleagues and savings and remittance bureau colleagues should work together. We are all one family and there is no boundary. We can take the path of cooperation and make solid progress, then the development of our entire postal service will be limitless. The situation of postal services in various countries is a clear proof. Today is the opening day of the General Post Office Savings and Remittances Bureau. I hope that the colleagues of the two bureaus can do it in this spirit in order to live up to the expectations of the government and the minister. I wish you all the best.

Japanese Decide on Countermeasures to Reclaim Navigation Rights 84

Secretly Increase Ships

Preparing for the Future

Reclaiming navigation rights and opposing mutual Sino-Japanese navigation are the greatest desires of Shanghai's Chinese shipping merchants. After issuing declarations and electing representatives, they presented requests to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Communications. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs also stated that it would never allow foreign ships to obtain coastal and inland navigation rights, and the Ministry of Communications sent the Navigation Affairs Department to Shanghai to discuss with Shanghai's Chinese ships the preparatory plan for reclaiming navigation rights, such as increasing routes, building more ships, and organizing new shipping companies. This is to avoid the lack of shifts and the disruption of transportation when foreign ships are withdrawn, which will hinder transportation and commercial transport. The Navigation Affairs Department has discussed this matter with Shanghai shipping merchants several times. As the military situation has not been settled, most of the Chinese ships have been suspended, so this case has also been stalled and has not been carried out. Now, the Sino-Japanese commercial treaty is being discussed, and the Japanese side has also taken some action on the reclamation of navigation rights. To the best of our knowledge, they are recorded as follows:

Page 18

Japanese Ships Urgently Seek to Add More Shifts: Sino-Japanese Renegotiation of New Treaty 85

The Japanese also know that our country will do its best to fight for coastal and inland navigation rights, which is inevitable. Since the Chinese oppose mutual navigation, it is difficult to find a win-win solution, and they have to rush to prepare countermeasures. According to reliable information from the Japanese side, the Japanese shipping merchants in China have secretly held several meetings specifically for this matter. It is reported that the Japanese shipping industry has decided on a method to extend the shipping industry in China. Taking advantage of the renegotiation of the Sino-Japanese commercial treaty, the Japanese shipping companies have decided to secretly increase ships in advance. For example, if the Yangtze River has ten regular scheduled ships, then add four or five more. The same is true for the coastal routes. After increasing the number of ships, it will be a countermeasure to our country's reclamation of navigation rights. If we raise this demand, they will sell all the ships to us at a high price to make it difficult for us, and then use the excuse of withdrawing ships in stages, which will increase the number of ships and extend the withdrawal period, so that they will have no losses in practice.

Dalian Actively Increases Ships: The Dalian Steamship Company will actively expand its Chinese shipping business this year. A larger new ship will be added to the Shanghai-Dalian-Qingdao route, which is larger than the Dalian Maru and Fengtian Maru, with a net load of 5,000 tons. The ship has been named Qingdao Maru and is reportedly nearing completion. The passenger seats and cargo holds have been enlarged. It is expected to arrive in Shanghai at the end of August and sail on the Shanghai-Qingdao-Dalian route. At the same time, the Sakaki Maru will be replaced and a new route will be opened to Shanghai-Hong Kong-Guangzhou. In addition, three ships will be added, which will be completed in September this year and used to expand the business within the South China Shipping Company. In addition, Showa Shipping has opened three routes this year, namely the North and South Ocean routes and the Yangtze River route. Recently, due to the large amount of goods in Wenzhou, in addition to the Lushan Maru, another ship, the Dongyang Maru, has been transferred to Shanghai to increase the Shanghai-Oujiang line. Since February of this year, the number of Japanese coastal ships has gradually increased, which has become a natural common rule.

Further Report on the Multiple Deaths and Injuries from Boat Collisions 86

Huangpu Ship Causes Six Deaths of Men and Women

Yesterday's report mentioned that Longshan Steamer of Sanbei Company and Huangpu Steamer of Taikoo Dockyard encountered accidents in the Huangpu River due to strong winds and tides. Numerous boats were damaged, and there were deaths and injuries. It is now learned that before the Huangpu Steamer had the accident, it sank a wooden boat in the Gaomiao section of the lower reaches of the Huangpu River, drowning five women, a very tragic scene. The circumstances of the two ship accidents are reported in detail below.

What Was Learned After the Longshan Steamer Accident: The time of the Longshan Steamer accident was around 11:30 AM. The affected section of the river extended from the Nisshin Company at Laobaidu in the north to the southernmost wharf of Nanyi Taixing in the south, a distance of about one li. More than 20 wooden boats in that section of the riverbank were damaged, and about 10 or more sank. Most of the boat owners have already towed the sunken boats to the beach. Among them, Sun Yugao's sailboat, carrying 21 tons of coal, is still sunk outside the Yitaixing wharf, with the mast protruding above the water. Xiao Chongming, a crew member on Bao A-xiu's foreign-style boat, saw the Longshan Steamer approaching his boat and tried to escape ashore, but was too late and was injured in the head. Afterwards, the water patrol police sent him to the Puxi Chinese Hospital for treatment. According to the boat owners there, a Ningbo Baiguan boat of a certain surname sank to the bottom of the river. All seven people on board fell into the water, and in the chaos, none were rescued. However, when inquiring with the water patrol authorities, they said that they had not received a report, so the truth remains to be verified. Others who were injured either went to the hospital or stayed at home, and the boat owners had scattered yesterday, making it impossible to investigate. It is estimated that the loss of boats and cargo due to the Longshan accident is at least tens of thousands of gold. After the collision between the Nisshin Company's Lushan Maru and the Longshan Steamer, the company unloaded all the cargo from the Lushan Maru yesterday for repairs. The export date of the 16th has been canceled. In addition, the stern of the Yangtze River steamer Dafu Maru, which was docked at Nisshin's No. 3 wharf, was also damaged when the anchor chain was broken when the Lushan Maru was hit. Fortunately, Nisshin Company sent workers to repair it overnight, and it was able to depart as usual yesterday.

Details of the Two Accidents Caused by the Huangpu Steamer: The Huangpu Steamer caused two accidents upon entering port, resulting in the deaths of six men and women. The details are as follows: (First Accident) At around 10 AM, the Huangpu Steamer was sailing into the Wusongkou when it reached the Gaomiao area of ​​Pudong. At that time, a Jiangbei boat belonging to Gu Rulong, carrying seven tons of Shanhe soil, was sailing upstream. There were eight people on board: Gu and his wife, two sons, and four daughters. The Huangpu was unable to avoid it in time and violently overturned the boat, causing all eight people to fall into the water. Personnel from the Mobil Oil Company in Pudong saw this and immediately dispatched a gasoline boat to rescue them. Gu and his two sons were rescued on the spot, but Gu's wife and four daughters had already sunk and disappeared. Shortly after, Gu's wife and his eldest and second daughters suddenly floated to the surface. The crew members on the Mobil boat immediately rescued them separately, but they had already died. The three corpses were transported to the Yinxianggang Wharf in Puxi. Gu's third and fourth daughters' bodies drifted away and their whereabouts are unknown. It is reported that the deceased Gu's wife, Liu, was 43 years old and from Jiangbei. Gu's eldest daughter, Guizhen, was 23 years old, his second daughter, Lao Er, was 10 years old, his third daughter, Xiao Lao San, was 7 years old, and his fourth daughter, Si Xiao Mei, was only 3 years old. Gu suffered this great tragedy of family loss and had nowhere to live that night, so he borrowed space in the Yangshupu Water Patrol Police Station. The three bodies recovered were sent to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall by Detective Zhu Yuncheng from the police station yesterday. The local court sent personnel to examine the bodies and then instructed the family members to collect them for burial and then file a lawsuit. (Second Accident) After the Huangpu Steamer caused the accident in the Gaomiao area, it continued to sail inward. Because the tide was high and the northwest wind was strong, it sailed to the Yangjiadu China Merchants Wharf upstream. It was about to drop anchor and turn around, but the hull was hit by the tide and there was no way to turn around. It crashed into the China Merchants Wharf, damaging the wharf. Several wharf boats docked outside the wharf were also crushed. Among them, Wu Zhangsheng's wharf boat, carrying 100 bags of white rice, was crushed. The cook on the boat, Li Genhe (46 years old, from Changshu), was about to run to avoid danger, but it was too late. His head was immediately crushed, and he fell unconscious on the boat. Several dock workers carried the injured person to the Pudong Hospital for treatment, but he died on the way. The hospital refused to admit him, so the workers carried him back to the dock. The body was exposed overnight until 4 PM yesterday, when no one had collected it for burial. The water patrol police sent Detective Cheng Yongnian to urge the family members to collect the body for burial. It is reported that the affected boat owners have asked the Taikoo Dockyard authorities to compensate for the losses and provide compensation for the innocent victims so that they can handle the funeral.

Joint Conference of Silk Weaving Mills in Jiangsu and Zhejiang 87

Telegram Urges Reciprocity in Chinese and Japanese Manufactured Goods 88

The Joint Conference of Silk Weaving Mills in Jiangsu and Zhejiang recently sent a telegram to silk industry organizations in Nanjing, Hangzhou, Zhenjiang, Danyang, Suzhou, Shengjing, Shengze, Huzhou, Shaoxing, Jiashu, and Shanghai regarding the issue of reciprocal tariffs between China and Japan, requesting them to jointly appeal. The text of the telegram stated (above omitted): "Reports indicate that the Sino-Japanese tariff reciprocity agreement involves preferential tariffs on Japanese manufactured goods in exchange for Chinese raw materials. This means that Chinese manufactured goods shipped to Japan and Korea will not receive the benefits of preferential tariffs. This will severely harm our silk industry. It is imperative that preferential tariffs be applied equally to both Chinese and Japanese manufactured goods, or to raw materials on both sides, in order to be fair and just. In addition to the efforts of this conference, the National Products Preservation Association, the Korean Chinese General Chamber of Commerce, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, and other organizations to strongly appeal to the National Government (telegrams already published in various newspapers), we urge your organizations to immediately respond and jointly appeal to save the silk industry and protect national products. We also hope that you will send a copy of the telegram to this conference." (signed) Jiangsu and Zhejiang Joint Conference of Silk Weaving Mills

Tariff Agreement Unrelated to Secured Loans 89

Yesterday’s Unofficial Statement from the Japanese Embassy

Recorded Here Pending Factual Verification

There have been misunderstandings in various circles regarding the Sino-Japanese tariff agreement draft, specifically regarding the case of securing Japanese old debts due to the ambiguous wording. Some have even suspected that future tariff revenues will be used as collateral for Japanese debts. The Japanese Embassy's office yesterday issued an unofficial statement to clarify these misunderstandings. The statement briefly stated that tariff autonomy in the Sino-Japanese tariff agreement draft pertains solely to tariff rates. In other words, the agreement applies only to tariff matters and does not involve other issues. Loan agreements are governed by their own provisions and are entirely separate from tariff treaties. Even if loan consolidation requires separate collateral, it will not interfere with the tariff treaty. In summary, the tariff treaty regarding tariff autonomy is one issue, and the consolidation of Sino-Japanese loans is another. Any concerns that the two are intertwined are unwarranted. (National News Agency)

Labor-Management Dispute Handling Law During the Transition Between New and Old 95

New Law Not Yet Promulgated

Old Law Should Remain Temporarily Effective

The trial period for the Labor-Management Dispute Handling Law expired on the 9th of this month. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs had previously telegraphed the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and requested the Municipal Government to forward a request to the Central Government to extend the trial period temporarily before the new law is promulgated to avoid a lack of legal basis for action. Yesterday, the Bureau received Municipal Government Instruction No. 3691, ordering them to acknowledge the State Council's telegram stating: "The Labor-Management Dispute Handling Law should remain effective temporarily under the old law until the new law is promulgated." The original order stated: "This government previously telegraphed the National Government and the Executive Yuan to request instructions on whether the trial period for the Labor-Management Dispute Handling Law should be extended and whether the arbitration committee could meet in the absence of an arbitrator. The State Council's original telegram stated: 'Regarding the requests for instructions, the President has instructed that the Labor-Management Dispute Handling Law has been revised by the Legislative Yuan and will be promulgated once submitted to the government. Before the new law is promulgated, the old law should remain temporarily effective. As for arbitrators, according to Article 15 of the current law, they represent each party separately. It is not appropriate to hold a meeting in the absence of one person.' This order is hereby issued to the Bureau for their information."

The Pharmaceutical Industry Dispute Remains Unresolved 96

Regarding the issue of placing unemployed workers in the pharmaceutical industry, a mediation meeting was scheduled for 1:00 PM yesterday at the Bureau of Social Affairs. However, the employers' association was unable to hold a general meeting and could not send representatives to the Bureau, causing the labor representatives to waste their time. The mediation was thus aborted. Both sides are arguing with each other in the newspapers, and the debate is becoming increasingly heated, making a resolution unlikely in the short term. The latest news from yesterday is summarized below.

The Workers' Union's Intentions Are Firm: The Pharmaceutical Workers' Union continued to hold a general meeting of members yesterday to discuss important cases. Their intentions are very firm. After the meeting, they went to the Bureau of Social Affairs to await the representatives' response. The number of people was more than 500, and the discipline was extremely strict. There was no shortage of people from various circles who came to express their sympathy.

The Association's Meeting Failed to Take Place: The Pharmaceutical Industry Association was scheduled to hold a general meeting of city-wide members at the National Federation of Pharmaceutical Associations at 1:00 PM yesterday afternoon. A large number of members attended. Just as they were about to start the meeting, a representative from the City Party Headquarters' Civil Training Committee arrived with an order stating that the meeting had not been approved by the Party Headquarters and could not be held. The attending members immediately obeyed the order and dispersed. The Bureau of Social Affairs had scheduled a mediation committee meeting for 1:00 PM yesterday and had ordered the association to send representatives. However, because the general meeting could not be held, the association could not send representatives. Therefore, the association appointed an employee, Mr. Wang, to the Bureau to explain everything to avoid any misunderstandings on the part of the Bureau. At the same time, they plan to follow the association's procedures and submit a request to the Party Headquarters for approval before notifying and convening a general meeting to discuss and resolve everything.

The Attitude of the Chinese Medicine Association: The Chinese Medicine Association sent a letter to the Workers' Union offering to mediate and willing to act as Lu Zhonglian. However, the Workers' Union declined, stating that they would wait for the higher authorities to handle the matter. The association also submitted a request to the City Party Headquarters and the Municipal Government, asking them to quickly resolve the difficulty of patients purchasing medicine.

Twists and Turns After the Resolution of the Xihe Yarn Factory Dispute 97

Party and Government Agencies Conduct Investigation

The National News Agency reports that the incident at the Japanese-owned Xihe Yarn Factory in Litanjiadu, where the factory arbitrarily reduced workers' wages, causing a labor-management dispute, was mediated by Tang Liqing, director of civil training in the Third District Party Headquarters. As a result, the factory fully accepted all 14 conditions put forward by the labor side, which the labor side considered satisfactory. Therefore, the dispute has ended. Unexpectedly, yesterday, some reactionary elements, seeing that the factory dispute had subsided and unable to cause further trouble, spread rumors that although the factory had agreed to the conditions, it had not posted a notice, making it difficult to trust. They incited the workers to resist with a strike. Some workers did not investigate the details and followed suit, causing a strike yesterday morning around 9:00 AM. The factory believed that the workers' conditions had been accepted in advance, and that the workers' unjustified strike followed, leading to misunderstandings. It was even rumored that the factory had announced a closure. The Third District Party Headquarters detected the incident and immediately launched an investigation by Tang Liqing, director of civil training. Section Chief Duan Wengong of the Sixth District Public Security Bureau was also investigating the factory. They consulted each other and held talks with both labor and management. It is reported that there is considerable evidence regarding the instigators of this dispute, which is believed to be the work of a few reactionary elements. It is planned to mediate immediately so that the majority of good workers will not be innocently affected.

Provincial Order to Implement Grain Storage 98

Regarding the grain storage affairs in Shanghai County, the Jiangsu Civil Affairs Department previously sent personnel to Shanghai to urge rectification. The county government also submitted the suspected grain storage assets to the Civil Affairs Department for review. It is now learned that the Jiangsu Provincial Government believes that some counties only store money instead of grain for grain storage, and this method easily allows unscrupulous people to misappropriate funds, creating loopholes. However, local grain storage is originally intended to prepare for famine and provide disaster relief and should be implemented seriously. Therefore, it has ordered the Civil Affairs Department to have all counties comply. The Shanghai County Government received the order and yesterday sent a letter to the Property Supervision Committee and the Property Department to implement it seriously.

Another Batch of Foreign Currency Arrived Yesterday 99

A large batch of foreign currency from India and Saigon arrived in Shanghai. The third batch of 8 million yuan of foreign currency was transported to Shanghai yesterday by a ship dispatched by a local bank to Wusongwai. Because it could not be transferred in one day, it was transported to Shanghai in two days. Therefore, there is still a batch of imports today, all landed at the Jianghai Customs Wharf, and then withdrawn and stored in the warehouse by a certain foreign bank.

Local News Two

Two Kidnapping Cases Solved Simultaneously Yesterday 100

Both Committed by Notorious Bandits from Jiangbei

The Old Case Involved Abduction and Rape of a Woman in Funing

The New Case Recently Occurred in Pengpu Township

More Than Ten Criminals Arrested One After Another

Liu Zhongyan, a local resident who works as a doctor, lives in a bungalow on the east end of Pengpu Bridge in Pengpu Township. Around 6 PM on Wednesday last week, he was suddenly robbed by Cao bandits, who also kidnapped his four-year-old granddaughter, Huizhen. Liu immediately reported the case to the Fourth District Public Security Bureau and requested an investigation. Chief Jin believed that this case involved both kidnapping a young child and robbery, which was extremely illegal. He immediately ordered patrol officers to lead the police and cooperate with all the detectives to solve the case quickly. They first arrested a suspected neighbor and then conducted investigations in all directions, sparing no effort. The day before yesterday, a Funing resident named Qiu Yinbiao reported to the station that his fellow villager, Hong Yinyuan, was a notorious bandit from Jiangbei. Two years ago, he kidnapped his sister, Xu Qiu, and his niece, Xiao Yatou, and secretly came to Shanghai to hide, raping his sister and making her his wife. It has now been discovered that the bandit Hong Yinyuan lives in Tanjiabao. He requested that police be dispatched to arrest him immediately. Upon receiving the information, Chief Jin immediately ordered detectives to go to the address and arrest Hong Yinyuan, along with Xu Qiu, Xiao Yatou, and three others. Xu Qiu finally saw the light of day after two years of suffering and described Hong Yinyuan's various illegal activities in detail. She also said that she had heard that Hong had kidnapped a four-year-old girl in the past two or three days, but she did not know where she was hiding. Chief Jin immediately interrogated Hong Yinyuan strictly, and he confessed to the kidnapping of Liu Zhongyan's four-year-old granddaughter, Huizhen. Thereupon, patrol officers, police, and detectives were mobilized overnight and searched the hiding places of Hong's accomplices, arresting more than ten criminals. Finally, at around 11 AM yesterday, together with Chinese and Western detectives from the Yangshupu Police Station in the Public Concession, they safely rescued the four-year-old hostage, Xu Huizhen, in a shack on Meizhou Road. Both the old and new kidnapping cases were solved simultaneously. What is particularly noteworthy is that the arrest of the bandit leader, the search for the accomplices, and the recovery of the hostage were all achieved without firing a single shot or injuring anyone. The details of the incident are recorded as follows:

Robbery and Kidnapping: Around 6 PM on the 12th of this month, that is, Wednesday last week, Liu Zhongyan and his guests were having dinner when six or seven bandits dressed in short clothes and speaking with a northern accent broke into the house through the back door to rob them. Because Liu's eldest son, Yinsheng, had just returned from Shanghai in his own chartered car, the bandits waited outside the house and were able to follow him inside. At that time, they took out their pistols and forbade anyone from making a sound. The bandits in the yard kidnapped Liu's four-year-old granddaughter, Xiao Huizhen, who was being held by his daughter-in-law, Guo. They also robbed the house of fox fur robes, fox fur jackets, gold rings, gold bracelets, and cash, worth a total of hundreds of yuan, and escaped. Afterwards, Xu immediately reported the incident to the Taiyangmiao police station of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau and requested an investigation. The Pengpu Township Defense Corps also arrived at the scene to arrest the bandits, but the bandits had disappeared without a trace. However, that night, the four suspected neighbors, Lu Zhengxuan, Lu Jinyun, Lu Zhengbao, and Lu Zhou, were detained at the station. The chief ordered detectives to work hard to investigate and solve the case as soon as possible.

Abduction and Rape: One day later, on the afternoon of the 10th, a Funing resident named Qiu Yinbiao reported to the station that his sister, Xu Qiu, had been kidnapped by the notorious local bandit Hong Yinyuan on the 10th day of the second month of the lunar calendar in the 17th year of the Republic of China (1928). His nine-year-old niece, Xiao Yatou, was also abducted at the same time. The sister's husband, Xu Yinshan, who made cakes for a living, escaped, but his house was burned down by Hong and he was left homeless. After kidnapping Qiu and Xiao Yatou, Hong Yinyuan secretly came to Shanghai at the end of the ninth month of the lunar calendar last year and committed rape. At first, he hid in Sanyang Road and later moved to the current address, Tan Ding Lane. Qiu Yinbiao came to Shanghai once last year and found out about it, but he did not dare to act rashly because he was isolated and weak. This spring, he came to Shanghai again with his sister's husband and found that Hong had moved to Tan Jia Lane. After a long period of research, he finally found him and asked the Fourth District Public Security Bureau to send police to arrest him.

Overnight Arrests: Police and detectives went to Tanjiabao and brought Hong, Xu Qiu, Xiao Yatou, and others to the station. Xu Qiu revealed all the details of what had happened. She also said that Hong did not return home on the 13th. The next morning, Hong's daughter-in-law visited and said that Hong Yinyuan had kidnapped a four-year-old girl somewhere, but it was not clear where she was hiding. When Hong Yinyuan was questioned, he initially denied it, then said that the matter was done by someone else and he did not know where she was currently hiding. After repeated questioning, he finally said that the hostage was now in Yangshupu, and then said that she was in Shenxinli, Sanyang Road Sanyangli, and other places. Police and detectives went to each of these addresses to arrest several accomplices. They also confessed that the hostage was hidden near Tanjiabao, or in a shack on Hutai Road, or in Jinxiuli on Guangzhao Road. They ran around all night, but there was still no news. They went to Yangshupu and other places two or three times or more.

Hostage Rescued: It was not until 11 AM yesterday that the real location of the hostage was discovered. Patrol Officers Gong and Xia, along with Detective Liu and Chief Police Jiang Zhuxian, went to the Yangshupu Police Station and explained the situation. They joined forces with Chinese and Western detectives from the station, fully armed, and rescued the hostage in a shack in the wilderness behind the Shuyuan on Meizhou Road. At that time, there were two old women watching the hostage, and there were also men and little girls at the door and in the room. When the police and detectives entered the door, Xu Huizhen was sleeping on the bed. The bandits seemed to have no defense, so the hostage was safely rescued and taken back to the station to be handed over to the victim. After interrogating the arrested bandits, they will be sent to the Judicial Section for review. The solving of these two old and new cases was extremely swift.

Child's Corpse Covered in Fresh Blood 101

Child's Corpse on Wasteland in Tilanqiao

Limbs Severed, Eyes and Nose Gouged Out

The Horrific Scene is Unbearable to Witness

Autopsy to be Performed at the Morgue This Morning

At around 9 AM yesterday, a nameless child's corpse, about five or six years old, was discovered on the wasteland near Ford Lane in Tilanqiao. Its limbs had been severed, and its eyeballs, nose, and tongue had all been gouged out. It was covered in fresh blood, a horrific sight. It was later discovered by Chinese Police Officer 1982, who reported it to the police station, and the corpse was sent to the Perrin Road Morgue. An autopsy is scheduled for this morning.

Case of a Maidservant's Poisoning: Master Accused of Murder 102

Suicide or Beaten to Death?

Plaintiff Requests Forensic Examination by a Western Doctor

Witness Claims Beating Over One Dollar

Master Recounts the Events Leading to Poisoning

Wang Wangshi, a 26-year-old woman from Anhui Province employed as a maidservant by Wang Senchang at his lumberyard on Xujiahui Road in the French Concession, had been working for only half a month when she allegedly committed suicide by poison on February 5th of this year. Wang reported the incident to the police, who transported her to the hospital, where she died. Her body was taken to the morgue. Upon reporting to the French Court, Judge Zhu arrived to inspect the body. The deceased's father, Wang Xunzuo, claimed that his daughter-in-law had been beaten to death by her employer. An order was issued for a forensic examination by a Western doctor. Furthermore, Wang Xunzuo claimed that he was too poor to afford a coffin and burial. The Tongren Fuyuantang charity was ordered to provide a coffin and arrange the burial. Wang Xunzuo then retained lawyer Li Shirui to draft a formal complaint to the French Court, criminally accusing Wang Senchang of murdering the maidservant and seeking compensation. Yesterday, a summons was issued. The plaintiff's lawyer, Fei Xizhen, argued that according to the deceased's family, the woman was beaten to death by Wang Senchang and his wife. Whether she committed suicide by poison or was beaten to death could only be determined by a detailed examination by a Western doctor. If the examination revealed suicide, the case would be closed. However, if it proved she was beaten to death, the defendant should be held criminally responsible and liable for damages. Witness Wang Deshun testified that the deceased was his younger brother's wife. Last December, he visited her and learned that the employer had held a gambling party, and a certain gambler won, giving the deceased one silver dollar. At that time, the employer's wife scolded her for keeping it all to herself and said she should share it with the nanny. The deceased was then beaten several times. He knew nothing else. Wang Senchang testified that the deceased had been working as a maid for only half a month. On February 5th, witness Wang Deshun arrived and went out with the deceased. They returned at 9:30 PM, and she went to bed. Around midnight, he heard groaning from her room. He became suspicious and knocked on the door. Seeing her pale face, he suspected something was wrong. He reported it to the police, who took her to the hospital, where she soon died. A Western doctor examined the body and concluded that she had committed suicide by poison and had not been murdered. He denied beating her and pleaded for a fair investigation. Judge Zhu dismissed the case and adjourned it for a future hearing.

Gang Fight 103

Harassment on the Road

Gathering a Crowd to Assault

Agreeing on a Time for Revenge

Multiple Arrests

A 15-year-old daughter of a man named Qian, residing at Zhu Jiajiao in Tangjiexi, Xujiahui, worked at a silk factory in Caojiadu, commuting daily. Recently, she was harassed on the road by a group of thugs on Haig Road. The daughter reported this to her father and brothers, who went to reason with the thugs. After mediation, the matter was settled. However, on the afternoon of the 13th of this month, at about 7:00 PM, Qian's daughter was returning home from work when the thugs drove up from behind in a rented car near Ligongmiao and slapped her several times. Unable to resist, she cried and went home. Considering the matter had been resolved, her brother felt it was wrong for her to be beaten again. Thus, on the previous evening (the 14th) at 8:00 PM, both sides gathered hundreds of people, armed with weapons, to discuss the matter at the Changchunlou teahouse in Xujiahui. Fortunately, the French police discovered this and sent detectives to arrest several individuals and confiscate numerous weapons. At the same time, the Second Precinct of the Sixth District also arrested a dozen or so people, while the rest scattered and fled.

Foreign Sailors Pull Rickshaws 104

Sailors Pulling Rickshaws in Public

Rickshaw Pullers Seated Grandly

Collision with a Car Leads to Negotiations

Paying All Their Money and Apologizing

According to the Shanghai Times, on Thursday evening, two foreign sailors on Avenue Edward VII suddenly had the idea of having rickshaw pullers sit grandly while they pulled the rickshaws themselves, parading through the streets. They were followed by dozens of curious onlookers. When they reached the vicinity of the Great World entertainment center, the rickshaw's shaft collided with a car in front, damaging its headlight. The car belonged to a French citizen, who became enraged and demanded satisfaction. The sailors repeatedly apologized, but the Frenchman refused and insisted on compensation of five dollars. The sailors emptied their pockets and found only eight dimes and ten copper coins. They were then taken to the French Concession police station. After much arguing, the Frenchman reluctantly accepted the apology and left with the eight dimes and ten copper coins. The sailors also returned to their ship, frustrated and no longer wishing to pull rickshaws.

Youths Distribute Reactionary Leaflets 105

Sentenced to One and a Half Months of Imprisonment Each

At 10:00 AM the day before yesterday, a group of young people calling themselves the "Propaganda Team of the China Art Vocational School" set out in formation with banners to give speeches in support of the unemployed workers of the Xiangchang Cotton Mill in the French Concession. The banners were made of paper and bore the words "Propaganda Team of the China Art Vocational School." They also carried two types of printed materials: a declaration from the general assembly of the students of the China Art University in support of the Xiangchang tragedy and a declaration from the representatives of all sectors of the Zhabei District in support of the Xiangchang tragedy. They distributed these materials along the way. As the team passed North Sichuan Road in the concession, a Japanese policeman from the 58th precinct of the Disweilu (Dixwell Road) station happened to be passing by on a tram. Seeing them from the window, he got off the tram and summoned Japanese policemen numbers 110, 128, and 93, etc. They arrested Zhang Wei from Guizhou, Zhou Tongren from Shandong, Luo Yiling from Hubei, and Huang Zheng and Zhang Yiming from Jiangsu, a total of five people. They confiscated six paper banners and one hundred leaflets and took them to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, Detective Wang Jie and Western Detective Esui escorted them to the Provisional Court, where Judge Wang Jianzu interrogated them. The police charged them with sedition under Article 103 of the criminal law. First, the Japanese policemen testified about the circumstances of the arrest of the defendants and presented the banners and leaflets as evidence. The defendants all stated that they were out raising donations to help the workers. After reviewing the leaflets, Judge Wang informed the defendants that they contained propaganda against the Three Principles of the People and were contrary to the policies of the National Government, thus violating Article 103 of the criminal law. He sentenced each of them to one and a half months of imprisonment and ordered the confiscation of the banners and leaflets.

Suspects in Reactionary Leaflet Distribution Case Await Transfer to the High Court 106

Patrol officers from the First Precinct of the Second District arrested Chen Ziqing and Zhang Daquan near Fangbang Bridge in Ximen on the anniversary of March 8th for distributing reactionary leaflets in public. They confiscated thirteen leaflets of two kinds and took them to the police station. It was discovered that the leaflets were printed by the Communist Party, and the language was absurd, inciting strikes. The defendants confessed that they were from Taixing and were hired to distribute these leaflets starting from Taixing in December of last year and all the way to Shanghai. The case was clearly reactionary and was reported to the Public Security Bureau. Yesterday, they were transferred to the District Court for a preliminary hearing, and an order was issued for their detention pending submission to the High Court for review.

According to the Da Wan Bao newspaper, the Public Concession police arrested a total of 318 suspects in various cases this week, with 107 being habitual offenders. The Municipal Government's Committee for Civilian Housing Selects Construction Sites in Various Districts 108

The Shanghai Special Municipal Government's Committee for the Construction of Civilian Housing is handling the construction of civilian housing. Previously, the First Civilian Housing project, consisting of one hundred units and a community hall, was built on Quanjia'an Road in Zhabei. The committee also designated the vacant land at the intersection of Xietu Road and Luban Road on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Bureau property in Nanshi as the site for the Second Civilian Housing project. Recently, for overall planning purposes, the committee selected four suitable locations in other districts of the city based on the number of shantytowns and the needs of the population: (1) south of Zhongshan Road, north of Zhonghua Xin Road, west of Changxing Road, and east of the Shanghai-Taicang Automobile Road in Zhabei; (2) north of the Suzhou Creek in Caojiadu and south of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway; (3) north of the Wusong Yunzaobang River and west of the North Sitang River; (4) east of the Caonitang River in Pudong. These six locations, including the existing First and Second Civilian Housing projects, have been submitted to the Municipal Government for approval. Construction will begin in sequence as soon as funds are secured.

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities Schedules Regular Inspections of Rickshaws 109

Starting April 1st

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities originally scheduled inspections of commercially operated rickshaws in the city four times a year, held quarterly. Later, in consideration of the rickshaw operators, it was submitted to the Municipal Government for approval to reduce the number of inspections to three times a year, starting this year. The bureau has now set the period from April 1st to June 30th for the first inspection of the year. The bureau has already issued notification forms to the rickshaw trade association and the North Shanghai Rickshaw Merchants Association, instructing them to properly allocate donation quotas and inspection dates and distribute them accordingly.

Conclusion of the Fang Family Inheritance Dispute Hearing 110

Discrepancies in the Testimony Regarding the Amount of Gold Pounds

Sentencing Scheduled for the 24th

Fang Dacang, son of the deceased Fang Danchi, claimed that after his father's death, the certificates of deposit worth over 200,000 yuan and gold pounds and gold leaves worth over 4,000 yuan were stolen by his father's concubine, Deng, in collusion with her father, Deng Guannan, and Wang Shutang, among others. He retained lawyer Zhan Jifeng and filed a complaint with the Provisional Court, which issued summons for Deng and her father. Wang also surrendered to the court. After several hearings, all of which were reported in this newspaper, Judge Luo Renxiang held another hearing yesterday afternoon. First, Wang Shutang, the owner of Jufeng Lumber, was questioned about purchasing a coffin for Fang Danchi. Wang said he used gold pounds as temporary collateral for the coffin price and later redeemed the gold pounds with cash. Then, Zhang A'gen, a tea server at the Hongkou Hotel, testified that the hotel's Room 19 was booked by a Deng surname, who went into the room with Fang and a child. The window of the room faced the street. Fang occasionally went out at night and did not return. The room had only one couch, and Deng also went out frequently, acting freely and without restraint. Judge Luo then questioned Deng about the number of gold pounds she possessed. Deng stated that her husband gave her eighty small gold pounds. After her husband's death, Fang Fengchi took away forty-four of them, so she previously stated that she had thirty-six. Fang Fengchi then entered the witness box and vehemently declared to the court that Deng's testimony was entirely false. He also recounted Wang Shutang's deceitful behavior during the funeral. He said that Wang had become friends with his brother and should not have acted in such a way before his brother's body was cold. He added that last October, Wang came to his house, and he sternly rebuked him, to which Wang remained silent. Then, Fang Dacang stated that Deng had told him after his father's death that she knew his father had a deposit of 30,000 yuan in the Siming Bank and 30,000 taels in the Meifeng Bank, proving that there was indeed an inheritance. Judge Luo questioned Deng, who said that she had mentioned the 30,000 yuan, but the certificates in the safe were taken away by Fang Hechi, who was now in Hankou. The court advised Deng that if she had concealed any property, she should hand it over, otherwise she would be held accountable if it was discovered in the future and could not continue to embezzle it. However, Deng insisted that she had not taken a single penny. Lawyer Zhan then stated that Deng had also told Bao Lingfeng about the deposit and could call Bao as a witness. Bao, who was present in the audience, immediately testified that Deng had indeed said at his home that there was a deposit of 30,000 yuan in Siming and 30,000 taels in Meifeng. She said that she wanted him to ask the Fang family for a share of the inheritance. She also said that the Siming certificate was red and the Meifeng certificate was green. The court then ordered the start of the debate. First, lawyer Zhan stated that Deng's statements were full of contradictions. For example, she initially claimed to have thirty gold pounds, then thirty-six, and finally eighty. This alone was enough to prove her dishonesty. As for the gold leaves, she never mentioned them. Wang Shutang's relationship was even more evident from his arrival in Shanghai this time. As a young widow, she did not stay with Fang's relatives but at Wang's home, which was self-evident. Furthermore, Wang Shutang's accounts did not match, and the Jufeng's accounting books were also suspicious. Deng Guannan appeared flustered when he met the plaintiff on the ship coming to Shanghai. Therefore, except for Wang Dahan, who had not yet been brought to court, the defendants in this case were guilty of joint theft and should be punished according to law and ordered to hand over all the account books. Next, the lawyers for Deng and her father argued that the plaintiff had not presented any evidence. If Deng had indeed stolen anything, she would not have returned to Huanggang. Finally, lawyer Jiang Yiping defended Wang Shutang, saying that Wang was only temporarily keeping the items and had already returned them, so there was no question of collusion in theft. After the arguments, Judge Luo announced that the sentence would be pronounced on the afternoon of March 24. Deng and her father and Wang Shutang were released on bail by their lawyers. Then, the lawyers for the Fang and Deng parties debated the cases of Fang accusing Deng of false accusation and Deng accusing Fang of obstructing freedom. Judge Luo granted lawyer Zhan's request to withdraw the false accusation case and set the sentencing date for the Deng case for the afternoon of March 24.

The Reason: Financial Difficulties

Feng A'long, from Yangzhou, was seen in the area of Fahua Township in West Shanghai the day before yesterday, selling a young girl. Connection Between Dismissed Maid's Theft and Extortion Case 112

The owner of a soy sauce shop in the French Concession, Zhang Zufufu, received several threatening letters last year and reported them to the police. However, the day before yesterday, a former maid, Yu A'cheng, broke into the soy sauce shop at night, intending to steal something. Fortunately, the shop's guard dog saw him and barked loudly, alerting the shop owner, Zhang Zufufu, who heard the noise and went outside to call for help. Yu was arrested and taken to the police station. Yesterday, he was sent to the French Court for investigation. A Mr. Jia appeared on behalf of the plaintiff, stating that the shop owner, Zhang Zufufu, was ill and could not attend. The defendant was arrested by the shop owner that night and asked what he was doing. The defendant replied that he wanted to borrow several hundred yuan. A piece of paper was found on his person, and it matched the handwriting of the threatening letters from last year. He asked for an investigation. Yu A'cheng confessed that he wanted to borrow money from the shop owner because he was poor. When asked if he wrote the threatening letters last year, Yu replied that he did. Judge Zhu ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody pending a future hearing when the plaintiff could appear in person.

Missing Girl Returns 113

Wei Youcai, a 44-year-old resident of the first house behind the Renjitang Hall on Xiaoxidajie, Shihuiyao, West Shanghai, had a daughter named Xiaodangzi, 17 years old. Her appearance was passable. She worked in a yarn factory. On the 18th day of the first month of this year, the girl suddenly disappeared without a trace. Wei searched everywhere but could not find her. Just as Wei was anxious, a Shandong man named Yin Baode, who cooked at the Public Security Bureau, came to Wei's house early this month and said that his daughter was now in Nanshi and that she could be found if a certain amount of silver dollars was paid. Wei immediately suspected that since he knew where his daughter was, he must have been the one who abducted her. He immediately turned him over to the police station in the Sixth District. After separate interrogations by Section Chief Duan, it was determined that Yin was suspected of extortion and was turned over to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation. However, the girl Xiaodangzi suddenly escaped from the buyer's house yesterday, intending to return home. Fearing being blamed by her father, she wandered crying on North Robertson Road in Caojiadu. She was spotted by a patrol officer who took her back to the police station in the Sixth District to await verification.

Married Man and Woman Seek Advice from a Boiler Shop Owner for an Affair 114

Claiming to be a Legitimate Couple

The Owner Acts as Matchmaker

Xiao Chen, the 32-year-old wife of Xiao Kuichen, who lived in Tanzwan, Zhabei, and was from Jiangbei, engaged in promiscuous love affairs with Zhou Sanyangzi. They were intensely passionate and wanted to become husband and wife for the long term. They asked Tang Weibao, the owner of a boiler shop, for advice. Tang devised a plan, telling the woman that she might as well run away and live with Zhou as husband and wife. American Professor Dr. Dutcher Comes to China to Lecture 115

Dr. G.M. Dutcher, a university professor dispatched by the International Peace Promotion Association, which was founded by the American steel magnate Carnegie, is visiting the world this year, including China, to give lectures. Dr. Dutcher is a historian with expertise in economics and politics. He is accompanied by his wife. They first arrived in Hong Kong and lectured at Lingnan University in Guangzhou for three days. From Hong Kong, they went to Fujian. Starting March 4, he lectured at Xiehe University for ten days on topics such as "The World Outlook After the European War," "The Foundation of the International Order," and "The Constitutional History of the United States." Next week, he will go to Shanghai to lecture at St. John's University and other places. Then, he will go to Nanjing to lecture at National Central University and Jinling University, and to Peking to lecture at Yenching University and Tsinghua University. After lecturing in China, he will go to Japan. The Fujian Provincial Government, the Department of Education, the YMCA, the Association of European and American Students, and the joint schools have all held meetings to welcome him. The doctor is 57 years old, but he is in excellent spirits and has a loud voice that makes his lectures engaging for listeners. He is scheduled to leave Fujian for Shanghai on the 14th.

Japanese Residents Demand an Increase in the Number of Japanese Police Officers 116

500 Additional Officers Within Three Years

Yesterday, the United Federation of Japanese Residents submitted a written request to the chairman of the Municipal Council, presenting three demands with justifications and requesting a response. The Municipal Council has agreed to submit the requests for discussion at the next meeting. The three demands are as follows: (1) The number of Japanese police officers in all police stations must be increased to 500 within three years; (2) The number of senior Japanese police advisors in the police department must be increased; (3) The authority of Japanese police officers must be equal to that of Western police officers, and their treatment must be the same.

A'fu Brought Back to Shanghai from Luodian 117

Accused of Raping and Injuring a Young Girl

With a Doctor's Certificate

Xu Xiangsheng, from Songjiang, and his wife worked in Shanghai, living at No. 1436 Zhangjiashe, Gordon Road. On November 4th of last year, A'fu, the brother of Xu's second landlord, Zheng Jinfu, took advantage of Xu and his wife being out at work and lured Xu's eight-year-old daughter, Jvdi, to the kitchen. He made her lie on a stool and committed a heinous act. When Xu and his wife returned home, their daughter told them that her lower body had been violated. They negotiated with A'fu, who promised to pay for the medical expenses, so they tolerated it without saying anything. However, A'fu later broke his promise. Xu filed a complaint with the Gordon Road police station. The police chief said that it had been too long and there was not enough evidence, so he did not accept the case. Xu was not satisfied and sent his daughter to Baolong Hospital for an examination. The doctor confirmed that the girl's hymen had been damaged, her vagina was swollen and red, and there was also swelling next to the pubic bone. There was also inflammation in the bladder. The doctor gave Xu a diagnostic certificate. Xu then retained lawyer Fan Gang to accuse Zheng A'fu of raping a young girl in the Provisional Court, requesting that he be punished according to law to maintain social mores and punish the wicked. A warrant was issued, but the defendant fled to avoid punishment. A warrant was then issued, and Chinese constable No. 2221 from the Huishi police station discovered that Zheng was hiding in Luodian. He reported it to the Luodian Public Security Bureau, who sent police to arrest him and bring him back to the police station. He was escorted to the court yesterday morning for investigation. The defendant also retained a lawyer to defend him, claiming that the defendant's surname was actually Jin and that the address was also incorrect, so he did not receive the summons. He also claimed that he was falsely accused in this case. When the defendant was questioned, he stated that his name was Jin A'fu, 40 years old, and that he worked as a bricklayer for the Municipal Council. The court asked him if he had any defense against the charges. Jin denied everything. Judge Zhou ordered the defendant to post bail of 150 yuan and adjourned the hearing.

Autopsy of a Man Killed by a Car 118

Zhu A'pin, 52 years old, from Ningbo, was hit by car No. 5251 on East-West Huade Road the day before yesterday afternoon. He was taken to Tongren Hospital by the police car, but he died. The hospital reported it to the Hongkou police station, who sent detective Xie Wanfang to take the body to the Feilun Road morgue. Yesterday morning at 11:00 AM, Judge Tan Xinzhen of the Provisional Court arrived at the morgue and confirmed the body. After briefly questioning the driver, Zhang Changgen, he ordered the company where the deceased worked to handle the funeral.

Commendable Courage of a Rickshaw Puller 119

Bandits Rob His Employer

The Rickshaw Puller Captures a Bandit

Yu Gengsheng, the owner of the Nanhua Sock Factory on Nanjing Road, was riding in his chartered rickshaw at 11:45 PM the day before yesterday when five bandits suddenly emerged from the darkness on Dagu Road and blocked the way. One bandit pointed a gun and threatened them not to make a sound. Yu also had a pistol for self-defense, but he did not have it with him. He did not dare to resist and allowed the bandits to search him, stealing a wallet containing 52 yuan in cash and three gun licenses. While the bandits were robbing him, Yu's rickshaw puller, Wang A'si, bravely grabbed the bandit holding the gun. The other four bandits then beat him. Although Wang's face and head were injured, he did not let go and shouted loudly. Nearby policemen heard the shouting and rushed to the scene. Fearing arrest, the four bandits fled, and the bandit with the gun was arrested and taken to the Lao Zha Police Station. He confessed his name was Wang A'er from Jiangbei. The police chief ordered him to be detained. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Provisional Court. After questioning, Judge Gao ordered him to be detained pending the arrest of his accomplices for further investigation.

Snatching Gold Ornaments from an Elderly Woman 120

Huang Huilan Sentenced to Two Years in Prison

The elderly woman Xu Wang was walking through the vegetable market in the French Concession the day before yesterday when the thief Huang Huilan came up from behind and forcibly snatched a pair of gold bracelets from her. Wang shouted loudly for help. Detective Mao Jingeng heard the shouting and rushed to the scene, intercepting Huang, and with the stolen goods brought to the police station. Yesterday, she was sent to the French Court for investigation. The plaintiff complained about being robbed. Huang confessed to the robbery without denying it. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Huang to two years in a Western prison as a warning.

Three Reports on the Murder Case on Xietu Road 121

Five Suspects Sent to the Bureau for Questioning

Qiao Shintang, the eldest son of Qiao Zhenyu, who lived at No. 1 Qiaojiatang, east of the Tianyao Bridge Road on Xietu Road in West Shanghai, was found dead. The case has been reported in the previous newspapers. The head of the Second Precinct of the Sixth District, Xu Yan, considered the case bizarre and brought Lin Sheng, the brother of Shen A'xiao, who drank with the deceased, Su Xinyi, Liu Genbao, who helped the deceased to Yongxingli and the Linxing Printing factory at midnight, and two women who had delivered clothes, Zhang Xiaomei and Shen A'bao, a total of five people, back to the station for temporary detention. The investigation is now complete. Yesterday afternoon, the suspects, along with the deceased's mother, were sent to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for questioning.

### Wang Yiting Appeals for the Disaster Victims 123

Submits a Request to Support the US Senate Proposal

Commissioner Wang Yiting of the Shanghai Office of the Relief Committee has repeatedly received telegrams from Henan, Shaanxi, Anhui and other provinces reporting on the disastrous situation, which is extremely severe. Representatives from Henan, Zhou Xiwen, Zhang Lie, Qu Wanshan, Song Guoliang, and Chen Linren, representative of the Henan Disaster Relief Association in Beiping, have also come to Shanghai to personally describe the disaster situation in various locations, almost tearfully. Commissioner Wang, being charitable and committed to relief, previously, together with Chairman Xu Jingren, repeatedly requested the government to continue issuing 10 million yuan in disaster relief bonds to facilitate spring relief efforts in various provinces. However, the Ministry of Finance stated that the bond fund was not available and could not be issued, and the committee had no large amount of funds to raise, causing deep anxiety. Seeing in the newspaper that the US Senate proposed allocating 25 million yuan to purchase relief grain for transportation to China for disaster relief, he wrote to Chairman Jiang yesterday, first stating the importance of spring relief and requesting the government to support the US proposal to allocate US dollars to purchase and transport wheat flour to China for disaster relief, to promptly bring the matter to a meeting and realize it as soon as possible. On the one hand, he requested that the Ministry of Finance allocate a large sum of money from nowhere to purchase seeds for distribution to various provinces for planting, in the hope of a promising autumn harvest. He also requested that the disaster victims in Henan Province be relocated to Liaoning and Ningxia provinces to cultivate wasteland and work as laborers, etc., as a fundamental plan for famine relief. In recent days, Commissioner Wang attended the Hua Yang Joint Relief Association, the Chinese Jisheng Association, and the Red Cross Relief Conference, and announced the severity of the disasters in Shaanxi and Henan provinces to the public, requesting the collection of funds for relief. The Hua Yang Joint Relief Association has allocated 120,000 yuan and remitted it to Henan Province for distribution by the association's branch. The Jisheng Association also plans to raise funds for relief in Henan, it is said.

### Latest Disaster Situation in Henan Province Received by the Jisheng Association 124

The Jisheng Association recently received a letter from the Henan Provincial Relief Committee reporting that the disaster situation in Henan Province is worsening, and the number of refugees is increasing daily. Currently, nearly 100,000 disaster victims are gathered in Luoyang, Zheng County, Kaifeng and other places, fleeing across the river. Because Xin, Mian, Luo, Yi and other counties still have roads to exit, while the traffic in Shaan, Ling, Wen, Lu, Bao, Yi and other counties is blocked, and about 5 million people are trapped and waiting to die. In addition, they have suffered from war, and more than 40 local counties, extending over 1,000 miles, have had their houses burned, grains and materials looted, with wails everywhere, food cut off, and deaths following one after another. Rescue is urgently needed, and we ask to appeal on behalf of the millions of disaster victims in Henan Province, to provide relief grain and relief goods to save their remaining lives, etc. The severity of the disaster in Shaanxi in recent years is unprecedented, and the current situation of the disaster in Henan is no less than that in Shaanxi. Millions of disaster victims are begging to appeal, hoping that charitable and benevolent people will broadly extend universal relief to save people's lives in the event of a disaster.

### Port Authority Plans to Dredge Wangjia Ditch in the Lvxing District 126

Total Expenses Required Exceed 7,000 Yuan

The Municipal Government Has Ordered Approval

Wangjia Ditch, a tributary of the Dutai River in Lvxing District, starts from the south entrance of Qianlangzhong Bridge and extends eastward through the 17th, 18th, 8th, and 11th districts, reaching the boundary of Chuansha County, stretching over ten miles. It is crucial for farmland irrigation and residents' drinking water. The river has been neglected for many years and urgently needs to be dredged. One section of it, approximately 1,580 zhang long, is particularly heavily silted and requires urgent dredging. According to the Port Authority's estimate, the cost of the project is approximately 7,000 yuan. In addition to the 2,000 yuan raised by the people in the district, the remaining 5,000 yuan has been approved by the Municipal Government, ordering the Finance Bureau to allocate the funds.

### The Municipal Health Bureau Formulates Measures for Donating Smallpox Vaccine 127

The Municipal Health Bureau, in order to promote the prevention of smallpox among citizens, has prepared smallpox vaccine for distribution to citizens. However, due to limited funds, it is necessary to impose restrictions. The bureau specifically formulated the following measures yesterday: (1) Due to limited funds, the donation of smallpox vaccine by this bureau must be restricted, and these measures are specifically formulated as a basis for implementation. (2) In addition to the sub-offices entrusted by this bureau to handle vaccinations, which are all supplied by this bureau, those who meet one of the following conditions may request a donation of smallpox vaccine from this bureau, the amount of which will be determined by this bureau. A. Hospitals or clinics attached to charitable organizations (must report the number of people vaccinated and return the containers). B. Public hospitals (must report the number of people vaccinated and return the containers). C. Factories and groups of more than 30 people, but must have doctors sent by this bureau to perform the vaccinations or injections. (3) Except for the places stipulated in Article 2, no donations will be made. However, formal organizations in this city that employ qualified doctors may apply to this bureau in writing for certification to purchase more smallpox vaccine at a reduced price from the Central Epidemic Prevention Office or this bureau's testing institute if they wish to vaccinate. (4) The A and B types of organizations in Article 2 must report the number of people vaccinated and return the containers when requesting a donation of smallpox vaccine next time. (5) These measures will be implemented from the date of their formulation.

### Japanese Aircraft Scheduled to Fly Back Today 128

The Sino-Japanese contact aviation flight has flown twice. Due to poor weather and the pilot's ordinary skills, the performance was not good. It is now scheduled to fly back to Fukuoka, Japan, this morning (16th). After that, it will be test-flown once every two days, postponed in case of rain.

### Jiang Sends Physicians to Bao to Prevent Epidemic at the Provincial Hospital 129

A meningitis epidemic has occurred in Yangxing Township, Baoshan County, and many people have died. This newspaper has reported on it. In recent days, the disease has also been found in Baoshan City, but its momentum is not as fierce as in Yangxing. Wei Bin, Dean of Jiangsu Provincial Hospital, has been ordered by the Ministry of Health, and on the afternoon before last, together with doctors Wang Xun and Dong Shi, went from the province to Bao to investigate the epidemic situation, in order to find ways to provide relief. County Magistrate Wu Jianong, First District Chief Sun Qixian, explained the process and circumstances of the epidemic and the epidemic prevention measures. Dean Wei said that Baoshan does not have a specialized hospital or excellent doctors, and epidemic prevention work will definitely be difficult. Therefore, Doctor Wang was specifically sent to stay in Baoshan temporarily to preside over the handling of epidemic prevention affairs. On the one hand, the county government and local gentry and businessmen will find ways to set up specialized hospitals, so as to obtain a one-time and permanent solution.

### Ship Repair and Towing News 130

Wusong Repairs Rudder Machine In recent days, due to the large and turbulent winds in the Huangpu River, navigation has been very difficult, and accidents have often occurred. Yesterday, the Taikoo Company's Yangtze River steamer Wusong, which came to Shanghai from Hankou, had its stern rudder machine leaves fall off and the ship lost its ability to move when turning in the river due to the turbulent river water. The company immediately sent a small steamboat to tow it into the dock, repair the machine leaves, and schedule it to open to the Huatong Wharf tomorrow to transport white sugar to Hankou.

Baling is About to be Towed Out The Baling Maru ship, which ran aground on Nanao Island, 25 nautical miles east of Shantou, has been rescued by Mr. Takeshita, the general shipowner of Nisshin, along with engineers, etc. Yesterday afternoon, Mr. Takeshita telegraphed again, saying that the rescue technicians and workers from the Tokyo Salvage Company who had been requested had arrived in Shantou on the tugboat Haiyuan Maru. From the 14th, the seawater in each cabin of the Baling Maru had been pumped out, the ship had been floated, the cargo had been completely lost, and the engine had also caught fire. A ship has been sent to Shantou to load coal, and as soon as it arrives, it can be towed to Hong Kong for major repairs.

### Chinese and Foreign Silk Merchants Discuss Changing the Silk Throwing Procedures 131

The Shanghai Silk Factory Association has recently requested that various foreign firms improve the silk throwing procedures based on the requests of local manufacturers. The chairman of the committee, Shen Huachen, visited Mr. Sha Guo, chairman of the Export Silk Association of Dachang Foreign Firm, the day before yesterday, explained the opinions of the manufacturers in detail, and requested that after the Chinese silk merchants delivered the future silk to the foreign firm, the payment should be made in advance, the silk should be weighed and loaded on the ship, so as not to delay the time. Chairman Sha agreed to convene the relevant industry members immediately to hold a discussion meeting, seek public opinion, and then schedule a joint meeting of Chinese and foreign silk merchants to jointly discuss improvement measures.

### Method for Paying Salaries of Customs Officers in Gold 132

Although the Gold Price Has Decreased, it is Still Calculated in Silver

The salaries of Chinese and foreign employees of the Jianghai Customs and the Dredging Bureau have always been issued according to Customs silver. Since the import tax has been increased in gold units, the salaries of all Chinese and foreign employees have also been calculated and increased in gold units. However, it is stated that this is an exception. If the gold price decreases and is equal to Customs silver, it should be cancelled immediately and still calculated in Customs silver.

Hai Rong, Pu An, Jian Kang

The Hai Rong warship of the Navy returned to Shanghai yesterday after escorting the Danish Crown Prince to Beijing. It entered the port together with the Pu An warship at 4 pm to be repaired. ### Municipal Public Security Bureau Requests Issuance of Official Passports 134

Since the abolition of the Diplomatic Affairs Office in this city last December, all passport matters have been transferred to the Municipal Public Security Bureau. Recently, the bureau reported that there are special commissioners from provincial governments or inspection commissioners appointed by the government who travel abroad in Shanghai from time to time and request official passports, which is very difficult to deal with. The bureau has approved it from the municipal government yesterday, requesting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to issue several official passports for filling in.

### Summary of Announcements by the Board of Directors 136

Wage for Russian Watchman Police It is hereby noted that residents within the concession who need to hire qualified watchman police may submit a letter to the chief of the police department of this bureau for approval and assignment. Those who need to be supervised by the police department may also do so. The monthly wages for Russian watchman police are listed below for your information: 65 yuan for newly assigned personnel, 68 yuan for those who have served for one year, 70 yuan for those who have served for two years, and 75 yuan for those who have served for five years. As for bank guards and private bodyguards, etc., you may also submit a request to the chief of the police department for assignment. The terms of employment shall be directly negotiated by the employer and the assigned person. This announcement is specially issued for your information. This announcement is dated March 13, 1930, by General Manager Edward.

Prohibition of Selling Game Cases It has been announced that from February 17, the period for prohibiting the sale of pheasants will be in effect. From March 1, the period for prohibiting the sale of deer, rabbits, partridges and all small birds will be in effect. As for turtledoves, quails, snipe, wild ducks, etc., they are not prohibited. This announcement is specially issued for your information. This announcement is dated March 13, 1930, by General Manager Edward.

The Third Day of the City Games P] 139

Yesterday's tennis and volleyball performances were excellent.

The situation today at the six venues for swimming, soccer, basketball, and other events.

The 15th was the third day of the Shanghai Special City Games. The ball game competitions included volleyball and tennis, held in separate venues, from 9:00 AM to 5:30 PM. The details are as follows:

Discontinuation of Group Tickets

The purpose of selling tickets for this Games is to subsidize the expenses of sending representatives to the National Games. This measure was originally a last resort.

The first two days of the Games focused on track and field events. The organizing committee believes that the Chinese people do not pay much attention to track and field events, which have repeatedly failed in the Far Eastern Games. Many

ate glutinous rice balls and left disappointed. Therefore, for this type of event, schools and organizations were specially allowed to visit to promote it. From yesterday onwards, without track and field events, all non-participating athletes and staff members must purchase tickets to enter the venue, so as to match the budget.

Not Many Visitors
